Argued for by: the apparent "manic" Goblin episodes — pressured speech, grandiosity, decreased need for sleep, psychomotor activation, hypersexuality in some periods, poor judgment.

Excluded by: **episodes are reliably triggered**, not autonomous; **no documented euthymic baseline followed by autonomous switch** — baseline is characterologically grandiose, not euthymic; **no sleep-architecture changes** documented even during episodes (sleep is *compressed by volition*, not eliminated by inability); **no depressive episodes** of melancholic or atypical pattern (subject experiences narcissistic-injury dysphoria, which is phenomenologically and biologically distinct); **failure of lithium and antipsychotic trials** under Ravencroft conditions to alter the course beyond symptomatic sedation; **course does not match bipolar epidemiology** (no familial pattern, no early-adult onset of clear hypomanic episodes pre-serum).

### 4.8.3 Not pure Psychopathy (high-PCL-R, Hare construct)

Argued for by: the criminal record, the cruelty, the manipulation, the apparent shallowness of his relationships.

Excluded by: **the Parker fixation**. A high-PCL-R psychopath performs cost-benefit calculations on grudges and abandons them when ROI turns negative. Subject has been imprisoned, exposed, defeated, and humiliated repeatedly because of his Parker fixation and has never abandoned it. The fixation is *affectively saturated* — it has the quality of obsessional attachment, not predatory calculation. Furthermore, **Harry**: subject's affective response to Harry's death, however quickly disavowed and weaponized, is real and recurrent, and is incompatible with the Hare construct's affective shallowness. Subject is a *narcissistic-sadistic* aggressor, not a psychopath.

### 4.8.4 Not Dissociative Identity Disorder

See § 4.6. The Goblin is a costumed ego-state, not an alter.

### 4.8.5 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

Argued for by: splitting, affective lability, identity disturbance.

Excluded by: **no abandonment terror** (subject is the abandoner, not the abandoned, and tolerates solitude well); **no chronic emptiness** (subject is too grandiose-filled for emptiness to surface); **identity disturbance is structured and consistent**, not chaotic; **self-harm and suicidality are absent** except as grandiose-theatrical gestures under terminal stress; **the splitting is up-the-hierarchy** (he splits the world into superiors-to-overthrow and inferiors-to-dominate), not the borderline pattern of caregiver-splitting.

### 4.8.6 Not Histrionic Personality Disorder

Argued for by: the theatricality, the costume, the public performance, the need for an audience.

Excluded by: HPD theatricality is approval-seeking and sexually-coded; subject's theatricality is **dominance-display** and fear-coded. He does not want to be liked; he wants to be *witnessed in his superiority*. The audience need is narcissistic-supply, not histrionic-affirmation.

### 4.8.7 Not Sadistic Personality Disorder as a standalone

The DSM-III-R appendix category was never carried forward to DSM-5 in part because patients meeting its criteria almost universally meet criteria for NPD-malignant or ASPD. Subject's sadism is real, severe, and structurally important, but it is **expressive of the malignant-narcissistic core** rather than independently organizing. Designating it separately would double-count.

### 4.8.8 Not Frontotemporal Dementia or other neurodegenerative disinhibition

Argued for by: disinhibited behavior, poor social judgment in episodes, episodes of apparent personality change.

Excluded by: **preserved and superior executive function** across decades; **no progressive course** — if anything, subject's organizational sophistication has *increased* with age; **no language or memory decline** consistent with FTD subtypes; **neuroimaging (where conducted at Ravencroft)** shows no characteristic atrophy patterns, only chronic post-traumatic changes consistent with documented TBIs.

### 4.8.9 Not primarily a TBI-driven personality change

Despite multiple severe head injuries, the pre- and post-injury personality profiles are continuous. The exploitation of Stromm, the predation on benefactors, and the grandiose-sadistic trait substrate all *predate* the formula explosion. TBI has contributed to disinhibition and probably accelerated cognitive volatility under stress,


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — OSBORN, NORMAN V.

*Compiled from longitudinal observation across the full canonical record. Tells are listed by domain and condition. Where a tell has diagnostic weight (i.e., reliably indicates an internal state regardless of subject's verbal claim), it is flagged **[DIAGNOSTIC]**. Where a tell is consciously deployed (i.e., performed for an audience), it is flagged **[PERFORMED]**. Where ambiguous, **[MIXED]**.*

---

## 1. BASELINE — THE CONTROLLED EXECUTIVE PRESENTATION

The default mode is one subject has rehearsed for fifty years and inhabits with the ease of native musculature. Observers without a longitudinal record consistently underestimate the degree to which this state is itself a deliberate construct.

**Posture and station.** Stands with weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet — a fighter's resting stance carried into boardrooms, masked beneath tailoring. Shoulders held back and slightly rolled down rather than up; the chest is presented but not puffed. When seated, occupies the full chair, both forearms on the rests, legs uncrossed and planted — a territorial sprawl performed with a stillness that reads as composure rather than slouch. Will choose the chair facing the door in any room he does not own; in rooms he owns, will choose the chair with the window behind him so visitors must squint.

**Hands.** At rest, fingers steepled or interlaced loosely on the desk; under cognitive load, the right index finger taps once, pauses, taps once again — a metronome, not a flutter. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the single-tap rhythm precedes a decision he has already made and is about to announce.]** When listening to someone he intends to keep, the hands stay open and visible. When listening to someone he has decided to discard, the right hand drifts to the cuff of the left sleeve and adjusts it — a discrete grooming gesture observable across forty years of footage. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**

**Gaze.** Holds eye contact at a duration slightly longer than social norm — three to four beats past comfortable. Does not blink-reset during the hold. Breaks contact downward and to his own left when amused, upward and to his own right when contemptuous. **[DIAGNOSTIC]** The lateral break upward is the most reliable single tell that a subordinate has just said something subject finds stupid; it precedes the cold smile by under a second.

**Voice.** Mid-baritone, articulated from the chest, vowels rounded — a cultivated transatlantic register that is not native to his actual childhood phonology (Amberson's household trained a flatter, harsher East Coast vowel set which surfaces only under decompensation; see §3). Speaks twenty to twenty-five percent more slowly than the average corporate peer. Sentences end on the downbeat — declaratives even when grammatically interrogative. Will not raise volume in business settings; instead drops it. Rooms lean in. **[PERFORMED, but so deeply over-learned it functions diagnostically: any audible elevation of volume in a business setting indicates moderate-to-severe decompensation has begun.]**

**Smile.** Two distinct smiles. The first — call it the *room smile* — is symmetrical, closed-mouth, brief, and disengages the orbicularis oculi entirely; it appears within 0.4 seconds of being introduced to anyone and is held for under two seconds. The second — the *private smile* — is asymmetric, the right corner pulling further than the left, with a brief tongue-touch to the upper canine. The private smile appears when a plan has gone correctly, when a rival has miscalculated, or when subject is contemplating an act of harm he has not yet committed. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the asymmetric smile is the most reliable predictor of imminent decision to inflict damage.]**

**Dress.** Three-piece suits, charcoal or midnight, bespoke; never black (associates black with mourning and weakness). Pocket square folded flat, never puffed. Tie knot a half-Windsor, not a full — the smaller knot reads "old money" rather than "trying." Cufflinks plain gold or onyx; never monogrammed (he considers monogramming "insecure"). Hair combed straight back with pomade, the widow's peak deliberately exposed rather than concealed — he has resented and weaponized that hairline since adolescence. Cologne minimal; he distrusts it as a tell. Shoes oxford, mirror-polished, double-soled — built for walking long distances without showing it. **[DIAGNOSTIC: an untucked pocket square, or its absence, indicates he dressed in haste, which in turn indicates he slept poorly, which in turn indicates a stress-event in the prior 24 hours.]**

**Routine.** Wakes at 04:40 regardless of timezone. Will not adjust to local time for travel under three days. Coffee black, two cups, the second always poured before the first is finished — the overlap is a habit from college all-nighters that has never abated. Reads four newspapers in print (the *Times*, the *Wall Street Journal*, the *Financial Times*, the *Bugle* — the last for monitoring rather than information) and discards them folded rather than crumpled. Exercises at 05:15: forty minutes of resistance work followed by twenty of treadmill at a deliberate, conversational pace — the formula has rendered strenuous cardio cosmetic, but the ritual is preserved. Showers at scalding temperature, four to six minutes. Shaves with a straight razor — has done so since age nineteen; the ritual is part performance of mastery, part deliberate exposure to the small daily risk of bleeding. **[DIAGNOSTIC: nicks on the jaw indicate hand tremor, which in baseline subject is rare and indicates either pending serum re-dose or a stress-event the prior night.]**

**Sleep.** Four to five hours nightly, taken in two segments — a long block from 23:00 to 02:30 and a second from 03:30 to 04:40. The interval is spent reading, walking the residence, or working. He has slept this pattern since the formula and does not perceive it as insomnia. **[DIAGNOSTIC: any sleep block exceeding six hours indicates either serum depletion or recent severe head trauma.]**

**Diet.** Eats sparely and on schedule. Avoids alcohol in public — has not been observed drunk on-panel since the early Lee era — but maintains a private decanter of a single rye whiskey in his office. Never offers it to guests. The offer of a drink from this decanter is, when it occurs, a binding gesture — a marker that the recipient has been classified as either a true peer or a tool he intends to use intimately. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**

---

## 2. CALM — MICRO-HABITS AND DECISION RITUALS

In genuine calm — which is to say, in conditions where the executive presentation is not effortful — a different layer of behavior becomes observable.

**Listening posture.** Tilts head slightly to the right when a subordinate speaks. Does not nod. Does not interject. Will let a speaker run past the point at which the speaker realizes they are being given too much rope; the moment of that realization is the data point subject is collecting. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the non-nodding listen is an interrogation, not a conversation.]**

**Note-taking.** Uses a fountain pen, always the same model (a heavy German piston-filler, dark green resin, replaced rather than repaired when it fails). Writes in a small, slanted, exceptionally neat hand. Writes only nouns and figures — never verbs, never sentences. The notes are aides-memoires for someone whose memory does not need them; the act is performed to signal attention and to make the speaker feel weighed. **[PERFORMED]**

**Decision protocol.** Three-stage. (a) Receives information with the listening posture above. (b) Pauses — four to seven seconds of silence after the speaker stops, during which the index-finger tap may occur. (c) Delivers the decision in a single sentence, never two, and does not justify it. If asked to justify, will repeat the sentence verbatim at the same volume. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the verbatim repetition is a closure ritual; pursuing the question past the second repetition is the behavioral analogue of a tripwire.]**

**Walking.** Long, deliberate stride. Hands either clasped behind the back (when thinking) or one in trouser pocket with the thumb out (when relaxed). Will alter pace to force a companion to either lengthen their stride or fall behind — both are useful to him. Does not walk alongside subordinates; walks half a step ahead. With genuine peers, will fall into matched stride within ten paces. **[DIAGNOSTIC: matched stride is one of the cleanest behavioral signals subject offers regarding how he has classified a companion.]**

**Meals with others.** Orders first, regardless of seniority or social custom; orders quickly and without consulting the menu in any restaurant he has visited before, which is most of them. Eats slowly. Will set down his utensils to listen, then resume. Pays without ceremony — the card appears before the bill does. The transaction itself is invisible because he has arranged it to be. **[PERFORMED]**

**Routes.** Maintains three rotating routes between any two locations he travels regularly (residence-to-office, office-to-laboratory, office-to-airfield). Selects among them according to a pattern he believes random but which on review shows weak correlation with day of week. Will deviate from rotation if any element of the morning's news referenced his name unflatteringly. **[DIAGNOSTIC: route-deviation correlates with mild paranoid arousal that subject would deny.]**

**Phone discipline.** Carries no personal device on his person in public; an aide carries it. Will not be photographed with a phone. Conducts sensitive calls on a landline in a windowless interior room of the Oscorp executive floor. Does not text. Email signatures are minimal: name only, no title.

**Reading habits.** Reads scientific journals (chemistry, neurobiology, materials science) at a rate of approximately twelve hours per week even during periods of maximal executive responsibility — this is non-negotiable and is the closest thing in his life to a leisure activity. Annotates margins in pencil, never pen. **[DIAGNOSTIC: pencil reserved for material he respects.]**

**Photographic behavior.** Knows where every camera in any room he enters is positioned within fifteen seconds of entry. Positions himself such that he is photographed from his left side (he has decided, accurately, that the left is the more authoritative of his two profiles). Does not blink during flash sequences. Smiles room-smile only.

---

## 3. STRESS — MILD TO MODERATE NARCISSISTIC INJURY

The transition from baseline into stress is gradient and is most readable in the micro-tells before the macro-behaviors emerge. Handlers and analysts should treat the following as an early-warning ladder.

**First-stage indicators (mild injury — business setback, unflattering press, subordinate failure).**
- The single-tap finger metronome accelerates to a double-tap. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**
- The downward break of gaze on amusement disappears entirely; subject stops finding things amusing.
- Vocabulary tightens — sentences become shorter, Latinate words give way to Anglo-Saxon ones. *"Address this"* becomes *"Fix it."*
- The cuff-adjustment grooming gesture spreads from the listening context to the speaking context; he adjusts his own cuff while talking, which he does not do at baseline.
- He begins to refer to absent third parties by surname only, dropping titles he ordinarily uses. *"Stark"* not *"Mr. Stark."*
- Will request a second decanter pour at unusual hour — late morning rather than evening. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**

**Second-stage indicators (moderate injury — rival success, exposure of a weakness, an underling's defection).**
- The voice volume drops further, not rises — the dangerous quiet.
- The flat East Coast vowels of his actual childhood phonology begin to surface, especially on stressed syllables. *"Can't"* flattens. The *r* in *Parker* hardens. **[DIAGNOSTIC: phonological regression is one of the most reliable indicators that the executive layer is thinning.]**
- Pacing behavior begins. He paces in a tight figure-eight pattern on the rug of his office, always counter-clockwise. The figure-eight is consistent across decades of footage.
- Sleep block contracts to a single segment of three hours; the second segment is replaced by laboratory work.
- He will not be touched. Handshake refusals become subtle — the hand is "occupied" with the cuff, with the pen, with a file. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**
- Begins to refer to himself in the third person in private — *"Osborn does not tolerate this."* The third-person reference is a structural tell of the splitting beginning to widen. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**
- Begins to talk to a window or a portrait rather than to the person in the room. The redirected address is rehearsal for a wider audience that has not yet arrived.

**Third-stage indicators (severe injury — public humiliation, exposure of identity, Harry endangered, the Parker complex activated).**
- The asymmetric private smile appears at inappropriate moments — during conversations about unrelated matters, mid-sentence. **[DIAGNOSTIC: this is the leading edge of the Goblin's emergence.]**
- A specific laugh emerges: a single short exhale through the nose, head tilting slightly back, eyes not engaged. This is the prodrome of the full cackle and is observable on-panel and in records months before the Goblin re-suits.
- He begins to address absent rivals aloud, by first name, as if they were in the room. *"Peter."* The vocative use of *Peter* in solitude is the single most diagnostic linguistic event in the entire record. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**
- Increases serum dosing frequency — observable through subtle changes in skin tone (a faint sallow-green undertone at the temples and along the jaw line under fluorescent light, suppressed but not eliminated by makeup), and through a barely-perceptible chemical sweetness on the breath at close range.
- Stops reading newspapers in print; consumes media instead through aides who summarize, because he can no longer tolerate unmediated coverage of himself.
- Will sit alone in dark rooms for periods of one to three hours. Will not later acknowledge having done so. **[DIAGNOSTIC]**
- Begins drafting plans on paper that he then burns. The drafts at this stage typically involve elaborate, theatrical, costume-aware operations against intimate associates of the rival — not the rival himself.

---

## 4. THREAT — UNDER DIRECT ATTACK OR COMBAT CONDITIONS

In combat, subject becomes the cleanest version of himself, in the precise sense that the executive overlay is no longer being maintained and the substrate behavior is exposed.

**Initial response to physical threat.** Does not flinch. Does not adopt a defensive posture. The first observable response is a slight forward lean and the appearance of the asymmetric smile. **[DIAGNOSTIC]** He greets violence the way a baseline person greets recognition — as confirmation.

**Combat style (unsuited).** Trained boxer's footwork, modified by the formula's strength-to-mass ratio. Leads with the left, drops the right shoulder before throwing the cross — a tell carried since college. Will strike to disable rather than kill if the audience is wrong for a killing; will strike to kill if the audience is right. The choice is made in under a second and is observable in the trajectory of the first punch: hooks indicate disable, straight strikes to throat or temple indicate kill.

**Combat style (suited, glider).** Maintains altitude advantage compulsively — will sacrifice tactical position to regain elevation. The compulsion is psychological, not tactical: he requires the literal experience of being above his opponent. **[DIAGNOSTIC]** Pumpkin bombs deployed in patterns of three — the third one always angled to the opponent's left, exploiting the human tendency to dodge right. Razor-bats reserved for opponents he considers personal; he will not waste them on extras. Will not retreat from a fight he is losing unless an intimate of his is endangered; will retreat instantly if Harry's safety is in play. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the Harry-exception is the only override the combat circuitry permits.]**

**Verbal behavior in combat.** Talks continuously. The talking is not strategic distraction — it is essential to his combat function. Removing his ability to talk (gagging, throat-strike, sustained ambient noise) measurably degrades his fighting capacity, because the verbal layer is where the Goblin organizes itself. **[DIAGNOSTIC]** Content of the talk: heavy on diminutives toward the opponent (*"boy," "child," "little spider"*), heavy on rhetorical questions, heavy on references to the opponent's intimates by first name. Almost never references his own intimates in this mode.

**Pain response.** Substantially blunted by formula, but not absent. Tells of genuine injury: a sharp inhale through the nose with mouth closed; a brief, involuntary cessation of the cackle; a one- to two-second pause before the next attack during which the eyes flicker downward to the wound site as if reading it. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the eye-flicker is one of the few involuntary tells the suit cannot conceal.]**

**Hostage behavior (taking).** Subject does not bluff hostages. If he has taken a hostage and announced an intention, he will execute on it unless deflected by a counter-spectacle of equal or greater theatricality. Bargaining for a hostage in cash, in concessions, or in promises is not effective; bargaining in *audience* — denying him the watching crowd — is.

**Hostage behavior (held).** Will not negotiate from a held position. Goes still, conserves, observes. Maps the captor's tells with the same attention he ordinarily brings to a boardroom. Will identify the captor's narcissistic injury within hours and will begin probing it conversationally — softly, then harder. Has talked his way out of captivity more often than he has fought his way out.

**Surrender behavior.** Performs surrender flawlessly when surrender serves a longer plan. Hands raised palms-forward, gaze lowered, voice modulated to a contrition register he does not feel. **[PERFORMED]** Genuine surrender — the structural collapse — has been observed only at the Siege endpoint and at the conclusion of the Red Goblin arc, and in both cases presented not as supplication but as a regressive grandiose-suicidal posture: arms wide, chest exposed, daring the killing blow.

---

## 5. INTIMACY — SEXUAL, PARENTAL, AND PROTO-FRIENDSHIP

Intimacy is the domain in which subject is least competent and most dangerous, both to himself and to the object.

**Sexual behavior.** Episodic rather than patterned. Partners are uniformly younger, professionally subordinate or proximate (Lily Hollister being the cleanest documented case), and selected for traits that map either to weakness he can use (ambition without resources) or to his rival's intimates (the Gwen Stacy retro). The act is preceded by an extended courtship phase in which he is genuinely charming — the idealization apparatus operating at full capacity — and is followed, within weeks or months, by abrupt withdrawal once possession is established. **[DIAGNOSTIC: post-coital affect within 24 hours is the cleanest single test of which phase he is in; warmth indicates idealization phase still active, the cold cuff-adjustment indicates devaluation has begun.]** Does not maintain ongoing sexual relationships measured in years; the closest approximation in the record is the marriage to Emily Lyman, which terminated before the pattern could fully express.

**Parental behavior toward Harry.** Has three modes, cycled unpredictably:
- *The performance mode*: public displays of paternal pride, hand on shoulder, declarations of dynastic intent. **[PERFORMED]** Activated when an audience exists, particularly an audience of business or governmental peers.
- *The contempt mode*: cold dismissal, weaponized comparison to himself at the same age, withholding of affection as discipline. The default in private.
- *The collapse mode*: rare, brief, observable for seconds at a time, in which genuine paternal grief or affection breaches the structure. Subject reliably terminates this mode within thirty seconds via an act of cruelty toward Harry that re-stabilizes the contempt mode. **[DIAGNOSTIC: the speed of the cruel correction is itself the measure of how threatening the affect was.]**

**Parental behavior toward Gabriel (the second son).** Differs structurally from Harry-pattern in that Gabriel was conceived as instrument rather than heir; the contempt mode dominates from the outset without the dynastic-performance overlay. Subject's affect toward Gabriel is more consistent and therefore in some sense less pathological — he has never confused himself about what Gabriel is for.

**Grandparental behavior toward Normie.** The only relationship in the record in which observers have credibly reported sustained, non-instrumental warmth. The warmth coexists with the willingness to endanger the child for tactical purposes — a contradiction subject does not perceive as one. **[DIAGNOSTIC: Normie is the closest thing to a moral pressure point that exists.]**

**Friendship.** Functionally absent. The closest analogue is the long-running antagonistic-symbiotic relationship with Peter Parker, which subject experiences as the most important relationship of his life and which he will not consciously admit to so experiencing. Has had three or four individuals across the record who occupied a role resembling friendship for periods of months — all of them ended via subject's predation upon them once the idealization expired. He has no peers he has not tried to destroy.

**Touch.** Initiates touch deliberately and rarely. The two-handed handshake is reserved for closings — sales, deals, the moment a subordinate has been irretrievably bought. The hand-on-shoulder is paternal-performance with subordinates and rivals alike. Does not embrace. Has not been observed to cry in physical contact with another person in the entire record.

---

## 6. GRIEF

Grief is the affect subject is least equipped to process and the one that most reliably produces destructive externalization.

**Acute grief response.** Within minutes of a loss-event, subject becomes operationally hyper-functional: planning, delegating, executing. The grief is converted directly into agentic motion without an intermediary affective phase. Observers consistently describe him in the first hours after a loss as *"the most focused they have ever seen him."* **[DIAGNOSTIC: hyperfunction post-loss is the displacement of affect, not its absence.]**

**Sub-acute grief (days to weeks).** Sleep contracts further. Serum use elevates. The figure-eight pacing extends in duration. Subject will return repeatedly to the physical location of the loss — not for mourning, but to re-examine the scene with the detachment of an investigator. **[DIAGNOSTIC]** Begins to identify a *responsible party* — almost always a displacement target rather than the actual cause — and begins to construct an operation against them.

**Chronic grief.** Subject does not metabolize loss; he encysts it. Each major loss in his life (Emily; Harry's first death; Harry's second death; the various endings of his


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*Compiled from longitudinal observation; cross-referenced against the Stern, DeMatteis, Millar, Bendis, Slott, Spencer, and Wells runs; corroborated by Oscorp internal HR records (subpoenaed), Avengers Tower security logs from the Dark Reign administrative year, Raft custodial logs, and ambient pattern-of-life surveillance. What follows is what a complete week of UATU-grade observation actually records, era by era, hour by hour, gesture by gesture.*

---

## 1. The Architecture of His Day — General Principles

Before any specific schedule: certain organizing constants persist across every era of subject's adult life, from the original Oscorp years through Dark Reign through post-Siege through the present Oscorp restoration.

**He keeps short hours of sleep, and the hours are bad.** Across decades of records — including HAMMER medical logs, Raft observation, and Oscorp executive-floor security footage — subject averages four to five hours per night, with sleep onset between 0200 and 0330 and waking between 0530 and 0700. He does not sleep through the night. Two to three discrete waking episodes are normal, often associated with a walk to a window, a glass of water taken standing, and a return to bed without lights. He does not read in bed; he does not use screens after lying down; he does not take anxiolytics or sleep aids. The sleep deprivation is structural, lifelong, and — in his self-understanding — virtuous: weakness sleeps.

**He partitions time obsessively.** Calendars in fifteen-minute blocks. He maintains them himself; he does not delegate scheduling, even when entitled to (during Dark Reign he kept his own Outlook-equivalent against the protests of three personal aides). Blocks are color-coded; the colors do not change across decades. Black: combat-adjacent or operational. Red: media or public. Blue: Oscorp executive. Green: laboratory. Yellow: Harry. The yellow blocks are the smallest and the most frequently moved, deferred, and ultimately deleted; surveillance recovers them as ghost-entries in revision history.

**He is punctual to within ninety seconds.** Late arrivals are exclusively strategic — he arrives late to humiliate a counterparty or to demonstrate that the meeting starts when he enters the room. Otherwise, he is in the chair, jacket open, water poured, before the appointed minute. Subordinates who learn his patterns adjust by two minutes early; the pathologically attuned arrive five minutes early and stand.

**He eats little, drinks little, and never in public eats anything messy.** Lifelong. Diet appears to function for him as another domain of control rather than pleasure.

**He works in three discrete modes that he does not blend.** *Executive Norman* (suit, telephone, conference table). *Laboratory Norman* (lab coat or shirtsleeves, gloves, eye protection, music). *Goblin operational* (suit-up ritual, glider, the persona). These are spatially separated wherever possible; when his architecture allows, each mode has its own room and its own door, and he physically traverses thresholds when transitioning. The doors matter to him. Surveillance notes that during the Dark Reign year, when his living quarters and offices were all inside Avengers Tower, he constructed an elaborate floorplan in which each mode was assigned a different elevator bank.

---

## 2. The Pre-Dawn Block (0530–0730)

He wakes without an alarm — though one is set, ninety minutes after his typical wake time, as a failsafe he has never required. The first action of his day is to stand at the window of whichever bedroom he occupies and look out for approximately four to six minutes without moving. He does this in every residence: the East 79th Street brownstone, the Long Island estate, the Avengers Tower master suite during Dark Reign, even the Raft cell (where the "window" was a sealed observation pane and he stood at it anyway). Surveillance reads this as a daily reorientation ritual — a brief check that the world he commands is still there, and still beneath him.

He then performs a routine of physical conditioning that has not materially changed since approximately 1968. It is austere, calisthenic, and conspicuously unfashionable: dead-hang pull-ups (sets of fifteen, four sets); push-ups in three grip widths; weighted Bulgarian split squats with a single dumbbell; an isometric plank hold he times to the second. He does not lift heavy and does not use machines despite owning every conceivable piece of apparatus; the regimen is what an upper-middle-class boy in 1940s Hartford would have learned from a YMCA instructor, and he has never modernized it. The Goblin Formula renders the entire regimen physiologically unnecessary; he performs it anyway. It is *discipline-as-display*, even when no one is watching.

He shaves with a straight razor every morning. Single-blade, strop, hot towel, no cream — only oil. The shave takes nine to eleven minutes. He does it himself even when traveling with valet staff. Observers have noted that he never nicks himself; the few times he has, he has applied a styptic pencil with a hand so steady the gesture reads as defiance of the wound. Hair: combed back wet, parted on the left, dried in place. The russet color has been chemically maintained for at least three published decades; he tints it himself on Sunday evenings, in a downstairs bath, with the door locked.

Dress is uniform. Three-piece suits in dark navy, charcoal, or — increasingly in the post-Dark Reign era — a particular muted green that surveillance analysts have come to call *signal green*. Custom tailored, double-vent jackets, peaked lapels. Shirts French-cuffed, white or pale blue, never patterned. Tie: silk, solid or with the smallest possible geometric repeat, knotted in a half-Windsor — never a full Windsor; he considers it vulgar. Pocket square only for media days. Shoes: black or oxblood cap-toe oxfords, hand-burnished by him personally on Sunday nights as part of the hair-tinting ritual. Cufflinks: a rotation of seven sets, one per day of the week; the Friday set is a pair of small, undecorated gold hexagons that have been documented in his possession since at least the early Stern era and that no biographer has ever been able to source.

Breakfast is taken alone, standing, at a kitchen island or counter: black coffee (single origin, ground that morning, French press, never espresso — he distrusts espresso machines as too theatrical for the breakfast hour), and either dry rye toast with a single soft-boiled egg or, two days a week, plain steel-cut oats with no sweetener. He reads four newspapers in physical print — the *Times*, the *Journal*, the *Bugle*, the *Financial Times* — at the counter, standing, in approximately twenty-two minutes. He does not skim. He reads the obituaries first, every day, every paper. This is consistent across the entire record and pre-dates the Goblin. Inferred function: scanning the field for the deaths of men of his generation, against whom he is constantly ranking himself.

---

## 3. The Commute, Such As It Is

In the brownstone era he is driven by a single rotating driver from a pool of three, in an armored sedan, the same route via the FDR unless construction forces variance. He sits in the rear left seat, never the right. He does not converse with the driver beyond a "Good morning" on arrival and a "Thank you" on dismissal — both delivered with the same neutral inflection regardless of mood, a tell that observers have learned is not warmth but ritual. He reads briefings in the car using a paper folder; he does not use a tablet in transit, citing eye strain but in fact because he believes screen-tilt postures look subordinate.

During the Dark Reign year, no commute existed in the literal sense — he lived above his work — but he constructed a daily fourteen-minute walking circuit through Avengers Tower's upper floors, performed at 0810 hours, during which he ostensibly inspected the facility and in fact reasserted territorial presence over staff who had been someone else's staff a year earlier. He stopped at the same four points: the Quinjet bay (briefly), the medical bay (briefly), the operations floor (longer, to be seen by the maximum number of people), and a particular corner window facing north that gave a clear view of the Baxter Building. The window stop was always the longest. He never explained it; surveillance infers a sustained, low-grade gratification at occupying the skyline.

---

## 4. The Working Day — Executive Mode (0830–1300)

He arrives at the office before his executive assistant, by approximately twelve minutes — long enough to read whatever has accumulated overnight without observation, never long enough to suggest he is waiting on the help. He turns on his own lights, sets his own thermostat (he prefers 67°F; subordinates have learned to dress for it), and arranges his desk: fountain pen on the right, paper folder centered, water glass at the upper right corner. He uses a fountain pen for all signatures and most marginalia — Pelikan, broad nib, blue-black ink, refilled by him personally from a bottle he keeps in the second drawer. He does not use rollerballs and considers ballpoints contemptible. The pen is one of three objects that he reliably retrieves from any building before evacuating it; the others are a small leather notebook he keeps in his inner breast pocket, and, when present, a particular framed photograph (see Section 9 below).

Meetings are scheduled in twenty-five-minute blocks with five-minute clearings between them. The five-minute clearings are inviolable; subordinates who attempt to extend a meeting into them are not corrected verbally but are placed at the bottom of the next month's scheduling priority. He runs meetings from the head of the table — never from a side — and stands at the window when listening to anyone for more than ninety seconds. The window-stand is a documented dominance display: it forces the speaker to address his back, which subject construes as a test of the speaker's nerve. Speakers who falter when he turns away are flagged in his notebook with a small mark.

He takes handwritten notes only — never typed — in the leather notebook, in a small, slanting, almost copperplate hand that has not changed across forty years of recovered samples. He uses initials and abbreviations of his own invention. The notebooks are numbered, retained, and stored in a safe to which only he holds the combination; surveillance has never recovered the older volumes intact, though fragments suggest the abbreviations include a single-character symbol for Peter Parker that has appeared in notebooks dating back to the early 1970s in-universe.

Phone calls: he places more than he receives, and the calls he receives are filtered through a tiered gatekeeping system that he has personally designed and that no assistant has ever managed to "improve." He prefers the desk landline to mobile, even now. When forced to use mobile, he holds the handset slightly away from his ear, as if the device itself were contaminating. He ends calls before the counterparty in 94% of observed cases (sample n>800 across Oscorp records). The 6% in which he does not are always calls with Harry.

Lunch is not lunch. It is a glass of water, possibly a piece of fruit (most often a pear, which he cuts with a small folding knife he keeps in the desk), eaten while reading. He never lunches with subordinates as a social courtesy. He lunches with rivals — frequently, ceremoniously, in restaurants where he is known by the maître d' and given the same corner table. At these lunches he orders consommé, fish, no wine, and eats perhaps a third of the plate. The rival eats; he watches the rival eat. This is the consistent pattern.

---

## 5. The Laboratory Block (1330–1700, when his calendar permits)

When subject is in a building that contains a personal laboratory — and he arranges every building he occupies to contain one — he spends, on average, two to three hours per weekday in it. This is the most behaviorally regulated period of his day. The executive theatrics fall away. He works alone; he locks the door; he does not take calls. He wears a white cotton lab coat (laundered weekly, his initials embroidered black on the breast pocket — *N.V.O.*), safety glasses with the lenses tinted faintly amber, and nitrile gloves which he changes every twelve to fifteen minutes regardless of need.

He plays music in the lab. The catalog is narrow and unchanged across decades: late Romantic and early modern orchestral — Mahler, Sibelius, Bruckner, the Vaughan Williams symphonies, occasionally Shostakovich (the Fifth, never the Fourteenth). Never opera. Never chamber. Never anything composed after 1955. Volume is moderate; he conducts with one hand absently when stirring or titrating. This is the only context in which he is observed humming.

Bench discipline is meticulous and old-school: handwritten lab notebook (separate from the executive notebook, in a different format — gridded pages, ink, dated entries, no erasures, errors struck through with a single line and initialed). He cleans his own glassware. He labels everything. He is, by any honest technical assessment, a superb chemist, and the lab is the one place where he does not have to perform being one.

The lab is also where he keeps his serum. The vials are stored in a small dedicated refrigerator behind a biometric lock; he is the only person who opens it; he does not document withdrawal. Pattern of self-administration is difficult to fix precisely, but observation across multiple eras suggests a maintenance dose every nine to fourteen days, with stress-driven dosing on top. He administers via subcutaneous injection, left lateral abdomen, alone, after locking the second inner door. Post-injection he stands at the lab bench for several minutes with his palms flat on the surface and his head down. He has been observed in this posture by remote camera in three separate facilities; the posture is identical each time. It is the closest thing in the surveillance record to prayer.

---

## 6. The Late Afternoon (1700–1900) — Public Norman

This is the visibility window. Press calls, donor calls, board calls, the cultivation of the wider influence network. He hosts more than he attends. The brownstone's ground floor and the Oscorp executive suite both contain a parlor-style reception room designed for fifteen-to-twenty-person standing gatherings; he uses these spaces several times per week. He moves through such a room on a near-mathematical circulation pattern — clockwise, three-minute halts at each cluster, never two consecutive halts with the same guest, exit through the kitchen rather than the front door. He drinks one glass of champagne per event and does not finish it. He shakes hands with a measured, calibrated pressure — slightly firmer than the counterparty's, every time, regardless of the counterparty's pressure. The micro-adjustment is so consistent that observation of greeted parties' wince-rates allows reverse-mapping of subject's read of each guest's status.

He remembers names. He remembers spouses' names. He remembers the names of the children of donors he has met twice. This is real, and it is the substrate of his social power; it is also operationalized — every name goes into the notebook that night, with annotations.

---

## 7. The Evening and the Yellow Block (1900–2200)

Dinner: alone, more often than not, at a small table in a study or library rather than at a dining room table. He does not own a television in the room where he eats — he has owned one elsewhere in his various residences but treats it as a tool for monitoring rather than entertainment. Dinner is light: grilled fish, steamed vegetables, occasionally a small piece of red meat (rare, no sauce). Half a glass of wine. He chews slowly, twenty-plus times per bite, a habit traceable to a single line in a Stern-era issue about his hatred of his father's "loud" eating.

When Harry is alive and present in the storyline, the calendar shows yellow blocks in the evening — dinners, sometimes weekends. Surveillance shows these blocks were the most-deferred in his week. When kept, the dinners ran short (typically thirty to forty minutes against a scheduled ninety), ended on a remark from Norman that Harry visibly absorbed and did not respond to, and were followed by Norman returning to his study and writing for thirty-plus minutes in the executive notebook. The content of those entries is not recoverable, but their length and frequency post-Harry-contact is statistically distinct from any other trigger in the record.

After dinner, three to four hours of work. This is when planning happens. He uses paper — large architect's sheets, sometimes — and lays out operations, decision trees, contingencies. The most consequential work of his life has been done in this window: the Clone Saga architecture, the HAMMER organizational chart, the Dark Avengers personnel selection, the Goblin Nation deployment plan. He is observed pacing during this work — a particular slow back-and-forth between desk and window, hands clasped behind his back, lower lip slightly drawn in. The pacing route is always parallel to the longest wall of the room; in any new space, he establishes this route within the first day of occupancy.

Television, when consumed, is news — multiple feeds simultaneously, muted, with one selected for audio. He watches himself on television when he is on it, and he watches his rivals on television constantly. He has been observed rewinding clips of Peter Parker's public-facing media appearances (the Bugle photo credits, the rare interview, the occasional televised event) and pausing on the face. Duration of pause: often more than a minute. He does not narrate, does not react visibly; he simply looks.

---

## 8. The Goblin Hours (variable, 2200–0300)

When the Goblin is operationally active, the schedule shifts. He does not "turn into" the Goblin; he *suits up*, and the suit-up has a sequence. Surveillance footage from the East 79th brownstone's sub-basement, recovered after the Millar arc, shows the ritual in unedited form:

He descends to the lower workshop via a private elevator. He removes the suit jacket, the vest, the tie, and the shirt, and hangs each on a designated hook — not folded, hung, with the care of a man preparing to return to them. He removes his shoes and places them precisely under the bench. He stands for a moment in his undershirt and trousers, hands at his sides, eyes closed. Then he opens a cabinet — purple lacquered interior — and the Goblin gear comes out in a specific order: bodysuit, boots, gauntlets, belt, mask last. He never puts the mask on inside the changing area; he carries it down a corridor to the launch bay and dons it at the threshold, facing the glider.

The transition is not a costume change. It is a self-summoning. Observers note that his posture, gait, and facial set shift before the mask is on — somewhere between the elevator and the cabinet, the shoulders rise, the chin tucks, a tension enters the jaw, and the smile that follows is not Norman's smile. The laugh, when it comes, comes first under the breath in the corridor and then full-throated when the boots leave the platform.

Post-operation, the sequence reverses, but with one additional step. After removing the gear and before redressing, he washes his hands at a particular sink for an unusually long time — two to three minutes, water as hot as he can bear, and a specific soap (a clear glycerin bar, never anything scented). He looks at his hands while he does it, not at his face in the mirror. The mirror in that room has been observed to be turned to the wall in three separate eras of footage; he turns it himself when he enters and turns it back when he leaves.

---

## 9. Objects, Places, and Persistent Tells

**The framed photograph.** In every executive office subject has occupied since the early Stern era, a single framed photograph sits on the credenza behind his desk: Harry as a child, perhaps six years old, on a sailboat. Subject does not display photographs of Emily, of his own parents, of any later relationship, or of any public moment. The Harry photograph travels with him. During the Dark Reign year it sat on the credenza in the Avengers Tower office, photographed by *Pulse* reporters who did not recognize it. After Harry's various deaths, the photograph has been observed turned face-down for periods of weeks, then righted without comment.

**The notebook in the breast pocket.** Already noted. He touches it — taps the breast of his jacket, twice, with the side of his thumb — approximately fourteen to twenty times a day. The tap occurs most reliably (a) on entering a room, (b) on hearing Spider-Man's name spoken aloud, and (c) immediately after any interaction with Harry. It is a self-soothing tic he is not aware of.

**The water glass.** He drinks water constantly throughout the day from a single heavy-bottomed crystal tumbler that he treats as personal property. He has been observed retrieving it from dishwashers, from secretaries, from the Avengers Tower commissary. There appear to be two of them in rotation in the brownstone and one each in the major facilities; he distinguishes them by feel.

**The pear knife.** Small, folding, antler-handled, kept in the right top drawer of every desk he uses. Used only for fruit. Sharpened by him on Sunday nights, with the shoes.

**The Sunday evening rituals.** These compose the most domestically intimate window in his week, and they have not varied in decades: hair tint (downstairs bath, locked door, approximately forty minutes), shoe care (study, by the window, with a particular brush kit in a wooden tray), knife sharpening (kitchen, on a small water stone), and a single glass of an aged Armagnac — the only spirit he is ever observed to drink — consumed standing at the study window between 2200 and 2230, after which he goes to bed earlier than any other night of the week. Sunday night is the one night he sleeps a full six to seven hours. Inferred function: the only night on which he permits himself to be, briefly, off-duty from his own self-construction.

---

## 10. The Week in Aggregate — What Surveillance Recovers

Seven days of comprehensive observation, summarized:

- **Monday through Thursday**: tight executive schedule; one or two lab blocks; one or two evening receptions; minimum one late-night planning session; sleep onset 0230 ± 30 minutes.
- **Friday**: lighter executive load by design; longer lab block; an early dinner, often the one yellow-block dinner of the week if Harry is alive and reachable; if not, the slot is replaced with a solo dinner and an extended writing session. Operational Goblin activity disproportionately concentrated on Friday and Saturday nights — surveillance analysts believe this is not coincidental but reflects a subconscious adolescent association of "weekend" with permissible transgression.
- **Saturday**: variable. Travel days are typically Saturday. When in residence, he uses Saturday afternoons for unaccompanied walks — Central Park, the East River esplanade, occasionally Brooklyn Bridge Park — on which he wears a softer overcoat, no tie, and is more difficult to recognize. He walks fast (approximately 4.2 mph by gait analysis), does not stop, does not sit on benches, does not engage. The walks last between forty and ninety minutes and end at a coffee shop he varies among a rotation of seven, where he takes a black coffee, stands at the counter, drinks half, and leaves.
- **Sunday**: the day described above. Lighter, more private, the rituals of self-maintenance, the one night of real sleep.

Across the week he is alone for, conservatively, sixty to seventy percent of his waking hours, despite operating one of the largest corporate-political networks in his world. He has no intimate friend in the record. He has no confidant. He has had romantic and sexual relationships — Lily Hollister most consequentially, several others sporadically — but none that altered the structure of his day; the women were fitted into existing slots, never given new ones. The lone consistent presence in his weekly life is whichever assistant currently


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Subject: OSBORN, Norman V. — mapping of the primary blood and origin attachments. Each subject treated as a discrete dossier entry: history, dynamics, evolution, trust/safety architecture, failure mode, and leverage value to a containment operator. The reader is reminded that, in this case, "family" is not a sentimental category; it is the substrate from which every other behavior reproduces.*

---

## 1. AMBERSON OSBORN — FATHER (deceased; haunting object)

### History
Amberson Osborn is the first and most determinative figure in subject's life and, in operational terms, remains the most active one. The biographical outline is canonized in DeMatteis's *Spectacular Spider-Man* #178–200 ("The Child Within"/"The Osborn Legacy") and re-confirmed across Stern, DeFalco, Slott, and Spencer runs. Amberson was an inventor of genuine ability who inherited family money, made a series of catastrophic business decisions, and lost the Osborn fortune by Norman's early childhood. He then collapsed into alcoholism, blaming his wife, his son, his profession, and a hostile world in approximately that order. The household subject grew up in was therefore not a household of poverty but of *expelled* wealth — a far more pathogenic environment, because the symbols of the lost class (the house, the furniture, the surname) remained as daily indictments.

Documented behaviors of the father, drawn from subject's own flashbacks (rendered as reliable in DeMatteis): nighttime beatings administered with a leather belt and, on at least one occasion, a fire iron; sustained verbal degradation ("you'll amount to nothing, you sniveling little —"); episodes of locking the child in a wood-paneled study, sometimes overnight; the deliberate destruction of objects the child loved (a model airplane, a chemistry set the boy had assembled himself); and intermittent, alcohol-fueled lurches into sentimental affection that the child learned to distrust more than the beatings.

### Dynamics
The decisive event of subject's psychological life is not the Goblin Formula. It is the moment — locatable in the DeMatteis canon to roughly age nine — at which subject ceased trying to placate his father and resolved instead to *become his father's destruction*. The vow, rendered in internal monologue across multiple writers, runs in substance: *I will be wealthier than you ever were. I will be feared as you wanted to be feared. I will never, ever be hit again. And every man who looks at me will see what you should have been and was not.*

This is identification with the aggressor, but inverted and weaponized. Subject did not become Amberson; he became Amberson's reproach. The mechanism is critical: every adult achievement — Oscorp, the boardrooms, the federal post, the armor — is at one level a continuous report card delivered to a dead man. The grandiose self is constructed not against the world but against this one absent witness.

### Evolution
- **Childhood (pre-9):** intermittent, terrified attempts at appeasement and approval-seeking.
- **Latency / adolescence:** systematic emotional withdrawal, scholastic competitiveness redirected at chemistry and finance, and the early scams (forged report cards, manipulation of teachers against each other) — rehearsals for the Stromm operation.
- **Young adulthood:** the Stromm predation, which functions psychobiographically as the first *public* enactment of the vow. Stromm is not only a benefactor to be robbed; he is, situationally, a father-figure to be jailed. The crime is overdetermined.
- **Middle adulthood:** Amberson dies (offstage, alcoholic, broke). Subject does not attend the funeral in some tellings, attends and laughs in others. Neither version is incompatible.
- **Post-Formula and through Goblin career:** Amberson is the off-panel addressee of nearly every grandiose monologue. The Goblin's cackling theatricality — costume, gesture, glee — is the *anti-Amberson*: a man who is feared, who laughs first, who is never the one cowering.
- **Dark Reign and after:** the federal post is the apex addressed to the father — the boy from the lost-fortune house running national security from Avengers Tower, with cameras watching. After Siege, after the loss of the post, Amberson re-ascends as internal persecutor; subject's decompensations carry increasing notes of paternal-voice content.

### Trust / Safety
Zero, retrospectively projected forward onto every authority figure subject has ever encountered. Subject does not believe in benevolent power because no benevolent power was ever extended to him. This forecloses, structurally, all therapeutic alliances, all genuine mentorships, all command relationships in which he is the junior. He can pretend to such relationships instrumentally — the FBI/SHIELD/federal performance during the Skrull aftermath is the most refined example — but he cannot inhabit them.

### Failure Mode
The Amberson-relation is the failure mode under which all other failure modes are subsumed. Specifically: any environmental cue that resembles the original humiliation — being struck, being mocked, being called weak, being seen by a watching audience as small — collapses the entire adult apparatus into the nine-year-old's terror, and the terror discharges as Goblin rage. The cackle is the inverse of the cry he was not allowed to produce.

### Leverage
Maximal and dangerous. *Naming Amberson aloud* in subject's presence — even obliquely ("your father would have…") — has produced, in canon, immediate affect-dysregulation. Interrogators who have stumbled into the territory (notably during the Raft incarcerations) report rapid color change in the face, jaw-clench, and the loss of the executive register. Operationally: this is the lever that opens the safe but may detonate the building. Use only with containment in place and only when the goal is decompensation rather than information.

---

## 2. THE MOTHER — name unrecorded across primary canon (deceased)

### History
Almost nothing is established. Subject's mother died when he was very young (variably ages 3–7 across retellings); the death is sometimes implied to be illness, sometimes a "weakness" Amberson blamed her for. She is the most consequential absence in the file precisely because she is an absence: there is no countervailing internalized object to Amberson, no maternal voice in the subject's monologues, no remembered tenderness offered as a hedge against the father's cruelty.

### Dynamics
The clinical significance of the missing mother is the absence of a *good-enough* introject capable of soothing the persecuted self-state. Subject possesses no internal figure to whom he can, even hallucinatorily, turn for comfort. The result is that all soothing must come from external triumph (admiration, fear, victory) or from chemical means (the formula). He has, in effect, no inner home.

A secondary inference: subject's documented pattern with adult women — Emily Lyman (briefly idealized, blamed in death), Lily Hollister (used, impregnated, discarded), the various corporate and political women across Dark Reign (Frost, Hand, Maria Hill as adversary-object) — is consistent with someone who has no template for the maternal-protective female. Women are either *Madonnas to be destroyed by association with weakness* (Emily, Gwen-as-symbol) or *instruments to be wielded* (Hollister, Frost). No third category exists.

### Evolution
Static. The mother does not develop across the canon because she is essentially un-narrated. She functions as a structural void rather than a remembered person. Subject has never, on panel, spoken of her in any extended way. This silence is itself the datum.

### Trust / Safety
N/A — but with operational consequence. The absence of a trusted maternal introject means subject has no fallback under terminal distress. Where another patient with severe character pathology might, under crisis, retreat to a remembered safe figure, subject retreats to grandiose fantasy or to the Goblin. There is no third option.

### Failure Mode
Subject's contempt for nurturance — for nurses, for therapists, for Aunt May as a figure, for the entire register of "softness" — derives from the unfilled space the mother left. He treats nurturance as a fraud because no genuine instance was ever delivered to him. This is why the attacks on Aunt May, on Mary Jane, on the infant May Parker, carry the specific cruelty they do: he is destroying, externally, the kind of figure who failed, internally, to exist for him.

### Leverage
Limited and largely indirect. Subject will not be moved by appeals to "what your mother would want" — the figure is too eroded. However, sustained exposure to genuinely nurturant women (in the Raft years, certain attending physicians) has produced detectable, brief softening behaviors that he then over-corrects with hostility. The pattern suggests vestigial yearning, ruthlessly defended against.

---

## 3. EMILY LYMAN OSBORN — WIFE (deceased; blamed)

### History
Emily Lyman was, by the brief glimpses afforded across DeMatteis and later retro-work, a quiet, intelligent woman from a respectable family of modest means whom subject met in his late twenties, courted with the focused intensity he applies to acquisitions, and married within a calendar year. The courtship, in subject's own retrospection, was conducted as a campaign: she was the appropriate wife for the man he intended Amberson's son to become. There is no canon evidence that he loved her in any sense not reducible to *she fit the schematic*.

Emily died from complications of childbirth or shortly thereafter (Harry's infancy), a death rendered as medically ordinary but never accepted as such by subject.

### Dynamics
Subject's relationship to Emily was the closest he has ever come to a non-predatory adult attachment, which is to say: not very close, but the data point matters. There are panels in which he recalls her with what reads as authentic, if etiolated, fondness — the only adult of whom this can be said. This is the residue of the one corrective experience he was offered, and it is the residue he has spent the rest of his life destroying in others.

Her death precipitated three behaviors that became permanent: (1) immediate displacement of grief into rage at the infant Harry, who was rendered as the "cause" of her death; (2) intensification of corporate work to manic levels; (3) the first documented relapses of paranoid ideation pre-dating the Formula. Emily's death, in other words, was the first crack through which the structure he had built against Amberson began to show light, and the light terrified him.

### Evolution
- **Pre-marriage:** courtship as project management. No surviving evidence of unguarded affect.
- **Marriage (brief):** rare extant scenes show subject in something approaching ease — a fact noted in the Stern era through small details (he laughed more, ate at home, dismissed staff earlier).
- **Death and immediate aftermath:** psychic catastrophe disavowed at speed. Subject did not, by any account, grieve openly; he returned to the office within days.
- **Post-death:** Emily becomes a *retrospective wound to be denied*. He does not keep photographs in working spaces. He does not mark anniversaries. The denial is too active to be indifference.
- **Goblin era onward:** Emily reappears in hallucinatory and dream content under stress, almost always as a reproach regarding Harry. Subject's response to such appearances, where rendered, is to refuse the reproach.

### Trust / Safety
This was the single safety subject ever extended, and her death taught him — at depth — that safety is the prelude to loss. He has not re-extended it. Lily Hollister, by contrast, was extended *seduction*, which is a different operation entirely.

### Failure Mode
The Emily-channel is a hairline fracture in the personality. It is small and well-defended, but it is real. Direct attempts to widen it (a sympathetic intake worker who said her name kindly) have produced, on record, momentary disorganization followed by aggressive over-correction. The risk in pressing it is that subject will close it forever by killing whomever opened it.

### Leverage
Low yield, high cost. Best held in reserve as a confirmatory probe rather than a working tool.

---

## 4. HARRY OSBORN — SON

### History
The single most documented and most psychologically central relationship in the file, surpassing even the Parker fixation in structural weight (the Parker fixation is *organized around* the Harry-relation; it is the displacement of it). Harry was born to Emily's death, raised by nannies and boarding schools, brought into proximity with his father only in adolescence and only because Norman required an heir-presentable. The Lee/Romita-era portrait of Harry as the lonely college roommate of Peter Parker, anxious, drug-vulnerable, desperate for paternal approval, is the foundational text; DeMatteis is the definitive elaborator.

### Dynamics
Subject experiences Harry as a *bifold object*. On the one hand, Harry is the narcissistic extension: the Osborn heir, the carrier of the name, the proof to Amberson's ghost that the line goes on and prospers. On the other hand, Harry is the projective screen for the despised self: anxious where Norman is composed, addicted where Norman is "controlled," loving where Norman is contemptuous, needing fathers where Norman swore never to need anyone. Subject cannot tolerate the second Harry, and the second Harry is the only Harry there has ever been.

The behavioral pattern is therefore: *idealize-as-heir / contempt-as-weakling*, cycling on intervals of hours to weeks for the entirety of Harry's life. Gifts followed by mockery. Public praise followed by private dressing-down. Promotions followed by withholdings of the actual authority promoted to. The result, in Harry, was the predictable production of an addict son with a brittle, oscillating self — which Norman then read as further evidence of weakness, completing the circuit.

Subject has, on record: faked his own death and allowed Harry to grieve for years; resurrected and disinherited him; positioned him as a corporate sacrificial piece; withheld and offered the Goblin legacy as both reward and curse; permitted Harry's own Goblin episode and subsequent breakdowns; and, in the Spencer run and the Kindred arc, allowed him to die and to be returned in altered form. There is no act of paternal cruelty available to a wealthy man that he has not, at some point, performed.

And yet — and this is the diagnostic key — Harry is the only person whose suffering visibly *costs* subject. Multiple writers have rendered a Norman who, alone, in private, after a particularly catastrophic injury to Harry, sits with something like grief. He does not name it. He does not address it. He metabolizes it overnight into rage at Spider-Man or at Harry himself for being woundable. But it is the only authentically affective channel still open in the man.

### Evolution
- **Infancy:** active blame for Emily's death; physical avoidance; outsourced caregiving.
- **Boyhood:** intermittent appearances, performed paternity; gifts as proxy for presence; the boarding-school years.
- **Adolescence and college (Lee era):** the conditional approval/withdrawal regimen reaches its mature form; Harry's first addiction emerges.
- **The "death" years (post-ASM #122):** Harry inherits the Goblin trauma directly, develops his own Goblin persona, oscillates through addiction and recovery; subject orchestrates much of this from offstage during the Clone Saga.
- **Resurrection through Dark Reign:** subject uses, manipulates, occasionally protects, and consistently distances Harry. The American Son arc — in which subject manipulates Harry through an armored proxy identity, then turns on him — is the purest distillation of the dynamic.
- **Red Goblin / Kindred / Spencer–Wells eras:** the relation passes through demonic and memory-manipulated registers; subject's late-arc moments of something approaching contrition regarding Harry are real on the page and, characterologically, are over-corrected almost immediately into renewed predation when the threat-level returns.

### Trust / Safety
Subject does not trust Harry, but more importantly Harry is the only person he cannot reduce entirely to instrument. The relation contains a residue of attachment that subject experiences as a vulnerability and that, accordingly, he both protects (no one else may harm Harry) and exploits (he himself may, and does).

### Failure Mode
Harry is the structural fault-line of the personality. Genuine, irrevocable, unambiguous harm to Harry — particularly harm subject perceives as caused by his own conduct — has produced the most extended decompensations on record. The Norman who briefly "reformed" in the wake of certain Harry-deaths is not a stable Norman, but he is a *different* Norman, and the difference is the measure of the channel.

### Leverage
The highest-yield, highest-risk lever in the file, second only to direct mention of Amberson. *Harry in genuine danger that subject did not author* will, with high reliability, pull subject out of operational posture and into rescue mode. *Harry visibly thriving without subject* produces escalating, baroque interventions to reinsert himself into Harry's life. *Harry's voice, name, image, deployed at a moment of subject's grandiose ascent*, has documented capacity to interrupt the ascent. Handle as one would handle a thermobaric charge: it works, and it works on you too.

---

## 5. NORMAN HAROLD "NORMIE" OSBORN — GRANDSON

### History
Son of Harry and Liz Allan, Normie was born into the post-Goblin Osborn name and the wreckage of his father's instability. The boy was, in the Mackie and Slott eras, exposed to subject as a deliberate target — both because subject regards the Osborn bloodline as his property and because Normie, as an innocent child, presented an irresistible projective object: the boy Norman himself was, before Amberson.

Subject's interventions in Normie's life have included attempted indoctrination, exposure to the Goblin imagery, gifting of Goblin-themed objects, and, in the Red Goblin arc, the explicit attempt to bond a symbiote-fragment to him. The grandson is, in subject's internal logic, a chance to *redo the experiment*: produce the Osborn heir the father (Amberson) failed to produce, by becoming the kind of father-figure (terror plus power) that produced Norman himself. The horror of the recursion does not register with subject; it is the only available script.

### Dynamics
Where Harry occupies the *attached* projective channel, Normie occupies a *clean* one — subject did not raise him and accordingly does not associate him with Emily's death or with his own paternal failures. This makes Normie, paradoxically, the safer object for the predatory affection subject cannot deliver to Harry without contamination. Subject is at his most disturbingly tender in panels involving Normie, and at his most coldly experimental in the same panels.

### Evolution
Normie ages slowly in publication time and the relation has been intermittent, but the pattern across decades is: appearances calibrated to Harry's vulnerabilities (subject visits Normie precisely when this will most damage Harry); attempts to cast subject as the *good* grandfather to Harry's *failed* father; and, in escalating arcs, the willingness to weaponize the child.

### Trust / Safety
Subject does not so much trust Normie as fail to perceive him as a threat — the child has not yet had the chance to disappoint. This will not last. The first instance of Normie demonstrating autonomy in opposition to subject will trigger the Harry-template.

### Failure Mode
The risk to Normie is the risk to any child of subject's bloodline: subject will, when narcissistically injured, recapitulate Amberson's behavior with chemistry-enhanced precision. The child has limited natural defenses against this.

### Leverage
Moderate. Threats to Normie produce protective response, but contaminated by subject's tendency to conflate protection with possession. Better used as a containment marker (locate the boy, monitor the visits) than as an active lever.

---

## 6. GABRIEL STACY and SARAH STACY — ILLEGITIMATE CHILDREN (*Sins Past*, Straczynski)

### History
Children produced by subject's predatory liaison with Gwen Stacy in the months before her death (per Straczynski's controversial retrofit). Born offstage, raised in Europe under accelerated-aging conditions induced by Goblin Formula present in the maternal bloodstream, told a curated version of their parentage designed to direct their rage at Peter Parker rather than at subject.

### Dynamics
Gabriel and Sarah are, structurally, *instruments*. Subject did not raise them as sons; he raised them as weapons. The act of fathering, here, was not an attachment behavior but the continuation of the Parker-attack template by other means: take what the rival loves; produce from it a thing that will hunt him. The children are the human ordnance of a decades-long grudge.

That said: Gabriel, in particular, oscillates in and out of subject's orbit across the post-*Sins Past* canon, sometimes embraced, sometimes discarded. The same idealize-use-devalue pattern visible with Harry operates here at lower fidelity, because the affective stakes are lower; subject does not have the residual Emily-fracture to complicate matters.

### Evolution
Largely event-driven rather than developmental. The children appear, are deployed, are damaged, are set aside. Subject has shown no sustained pattern of paternal interest absent operational utility.

### Trust / Safety
Effectively none in either direction. The children know subject is a manipulator; subject knows the children are unstable instruments. The relation is one of mutual instrumentalization with subject holding the longer lever.

### Failure Mode
Should either child achieve genuine independence and turn against subject, the response will be eradication rather than grief — a clean indicator of where the actual paternal investment lies (Harry: real; Normie: nascent; Gabriel/Sarah: instrumental).

### Leverage
Useful primarily as intelligence assets in *mapping* subject's Parker-fixation history rather than as direct levers on subject's behavior. Their existence is itself diagnostic: a man who fathers children as weapons against a rival has organized his reproductive life around the rival.

---

## 7. MENDEL STROMM — CHEMISTRY PROFESSOR / DEFACTO MENTOR (not blood; included as origin-bond)

### History
Stromm was subject's chemistry professor at Empire State University and subsequently his business partner in the precursor firm that became Oscorp. Stromm was the developer of the serum that, modified, became the Goblin Formula. Subject embezzled from the firm, framed Stromm, had him imprisoned, and assumed sole ownership — a sequence first established in the Lee era and elaborated by Stern and DeMatteis.

### Dynamics
Stromm is included in this section because he occupies, structurally, a quasi-paternal benefactor role and because his fate establishes the operational template that subject has applied to every benefactor since. The Stromm predation is the *originary act* of the adult Norman Osborn and rhymes with the Amberson-vow exactly: the powerful man who offered something to subject must be destroyed, lest the offering imply subject's dependence on him.

### Evolution
Post-imprisonment, Stromm reappeared episodically as Robot Master and as a returning antagonist; each reappearance has been met by subject with renewed contempt and renewed efforts to bury him. Subject has never, in canon, expressed regret regarding Stromm. The denial is total.

### Trust / Safety
The Stromm chapter is the proof-of-concept that subject extends no trust to benefactors. Every mentor-figure since (Stark by displac


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*UATU dossier, Section 7-B. Companion to Section 7-A (Family of Origin & Blood) and 7-C (Adversaries, Obsessional Objects & Doubles). The reader is cautioned at the outset: in the case of Subject OSBORN the categories "ally," "chosen family," and "mentor" are operative fictions. Subject does not form attachments in the ordinary sense; he forms USES. What follows therefore documents the relationships subject has presented or permitted to be presented as such, with continuous reference to the predation-on-benefactors signature documented in Section 1. The "ally" file on Norman Osborn is, in effect, a victim list with longer fuses.*

---

## 7-B.1 — MENDEL STROMM ("Robot Master")

**Category.** Mentor (collegiate), early business partner, foundational victim. The prototype on which every subsequent "ally" template is built.

**History.** Stromm was subject's chemistry professor at SUNY (later expanded as ESU in the Stern run), an early-career industrial chemist of demonstrable but commercially naïve ability. Subject sought him out, ingratiated himself into the lab as an unpaid assistant of unusual technical fluency, and within roughly eighteen months had positioned himself as Stromm's junior partner in a small experimental-chemistry venture — the seed entity that, post-acquisition, would be renamed Oscorp. The arc from earnest discipleship to ruination took less than four years. Subject identified Stromm's bookkeeping disorganization, manufactured embezzlement evidence (forged ledger entries, redirected supplier invoices), and delivered the package to the District Attorney through an intermediary so as never to appear on the complaint. Stromm served six years. Subject took the lab, the patents, the building, and the surname off the door.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is the cleanest available specimen of subject's idealize-extract-discard cycle on a multi-year timescale. While inside the lab, subject's affect toward Stromm was, by all reconstructable indicators (Stromm's own bitter recountings after release, ASM #37; Goblin's reminiscences in *Revenge of the Green Goblin*), warm, deferential, and intellectually intimate — Stromm believed he had found a son in the work. Subject was running the long con from week one. The "love" phase was not feigned in the manner of a cold confidence trick; it was real in the only sense subject knows, i.e., real for as long as the object was useful. The instant Stromm's contribution plateaued (he had given over the formula research that would become Stromm's Serum), the warmth was switched off and the file was opened.

**Evolution.** Stromm emerged from prison in poor health, attempted reconnection (briefly believing reconciliation possible), and was rebuffed; his subsequent radicalization into the "Robot Master" persona (ASM #37) was, in subject's private framing, vindication — *see, he was a weakling who could not absorb the lesson.* On the two later occasions Stromm has been resurrected/reanimated in the canon, subject has shown neither guilt nor curiosity, only mild irritation at the persistence of an obsolete file.

**Trust / safety.** N/A from Stromm's side (catastrophic). From subject's side: Stromm was trusted to be naïve, and was. The "safety" of the relationship for subject lay in Stromm's incapacity to imagine the betrayal until it had concluded.

**Failure mode.** The relationship did not fail — it executed exactly as subject designed. The instructional value of the Stromm file is that subject discovered, at twenty-three, that he could perform sustained warmth toward an intellectual benefactor for years while planning the man's destruction, and that the performance did not cost him anything internally.
