Every subsequent "mentor" or "partner" relationship is run from this playbook.

**Leverage.** Posthumous and instructional only. For containment purposes, Stromm is most useful as the template by which subject's current "warm" relationships should be read: assume duration is a function of remaining extractable value, not of bond.

---

## 7-B.2 — J. JONAH JAMESON (anomalous category: hostile-collegial)

**Category.** Public peer, civic rival, briefly subordinated (Pulse / Daily Bugle acquisition arc). Included here because subject has, in his own internal taxonomy, treated Jameson as something nearer an equal than almost any other living non-superhuman.

**History.** Two New York industrial-class men of overlapping generation, overlapping clubs (the Century, the Cattleman's, the older Wall Street luncheon circuit pre-1990), overlapping charitable boards (Met Museum trustees in the late 80s; both resigned within a year of each other for unrelated reasons). They were never friends. They were, for thirty years, the kind of acquaintances who know each other's secretaries by name. Subject acquired the Daily Bugle during the Stern/Mackie corporate arc explicitly to humiliate Jameson — the press baron reduced to employee of the man whose son had married Jameson's circle.

**Dynamics.** Subject recognizes in Jameson something he does not recognize in many men: an antagonist whose contempt is not pretense. Jameson is not afraid of him; Jameson dislikes him on the merits. This is *legible* to subject in a way that is almost flattering. Most of subject's social world either fears him or flatters him; Jameson treats him as a peer-shaped problem. There is, accordingly, a peculiar restraint in subject's conduct toward Jameson — the Goblin has had multiple opportunities to murder him and has not. The most plausible inference: Jameson is one of the very few witnesses whose continued existence ratifies subject's importance.

**Evolution.** From cordial-cold acquaintance (1970s) → through proxy-conflict via Spider-Man's reportage (1980s) → through direct corporate attack and acquisition (1990s) → through Dark Reign, in which Jameson as Mayor of New York City became one of the few public figures whose denunciations of subject carried weight subject could not dismiss. Subject's response to Mayor Jameson in *Dark Reign / Siege* was characteristic: surveillance, intimidation through HAMMER assets, and a refusal to authorize direct elimination that subject's own staff (Hood, Bullseye) repeatedly proposed.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric and stable. Jameson trusts subject to behave exactly as subject behaves; subject trusts Jameson to make noise but not to physically threaten. The relationship is paradoxically the most predictable on subject's social ledger.

**Failure mode.** Jameson will not be flipped, bought, or seduced — three decades have demonstrated this. The failure mode is that subject, under terminal narcissistic injury, will eventually attempt to kill him and fail noisily, having burned operational capital on a target who is not the actual rival.

**Leverage.** For a containing institution, Jameson is irreplaceable: a man immune to subject's primary manipulative grammars (flattery, money, fear of cancellation), with thirty years of contextual knowledge. Should be debriefed extensively; should be protected continuously.

---

## 7-B.3 — DR. ASHLEY KAFKA (anomalous category: imposed-therapist becoming pseudo-confidante)

**Category.** Court-mandated forensic psychiatrist, Ravencroft Institute (post-*Pulse*, through DeMatteis and Slott runs). Included because subject permitted with her a degree of disclosure he has permitted with no other living person.

**History.** Kafka was assigned to subject during multiple involuntary commitments and pre-trial evaluations spanning approximately fifteen years of in-universe time. Subject's initial posture was the standard malingering-and-charm-offensive he runs on all forensic clinicians (cooperative, articulate, mildly insight-performative, calibrated to suggest treatability without conceding pathology). Kafka, unusually, did not flatter back, did not pretend to believe him, and did not become afraid. Over the second and third years of intermittent contact, subject's posture shifted: he began to *talk*. About Amberson. About Emily. About the inside of his head during the Goblin states. Not all of it true — much of it instrumental — but a non-zero residue of disclosure that, in context, is unprecedented.

**Dynamics.** Subject experienced Kafka as a controlled audience whose containment of his disclosure was guaranteed by professional structure. This permitted a regulated version of the spectacle-need (see Section 5: he requires witnesses) without the risk of public exposure. Kafka, for her part, appears to have understood — and to have used — that she was being permitted access on those terms, and to have extracted real clinical material within them. The relationship was the closest thing to a therapeutic alliance subject has ever sustained, and even so it was, on his side, a managed performance with occasional unmanaged moments.

**Evolution.** Steady, then catastrophic. Kafka's murder (during the *Spider-Man: The Clone Conspiracy* / *Carnage* arcs, killed not directly by subject but by a Carnage proxy in subject's environment) closed the file with the canonical signature of every Osborn intimate: she ended dead, and subject metabolized it within hours.

**Trust / safety.** Subject trusted Kafka within the narrow channel of her professional role and not beyond it. He did not threaten her, did not seduce her, did not attempt to corrupt her — which, for subject, is an entire dialect of respect.

**Failure mode.** Proximity. Anyone who occupies a sustained, semi-intimate position in subject's life is in the kill-radius of his enemies, his subordinates, his serum, and ultimately himself.

**Leverage.** Kafka's case notes (if recoverable) are the highest-value clinical document in the file. Her successor in any containment regime should be selected on the Kafka template: non-flattering, non-fearful, non-seductive, professionally rigid, and physically protected as a high-value target.

---

## 7-B.4 — DONALD MENKEN

**Category.** Senior Oscorp executive, longest-serving subordinate, the closest analogue to a "consigliere" in subject's working life. Appears across Stern, DeFalco, Slott runs; central in *Superior Spider-Man / Goblin Nation*.

**History.** Menken entered Oscorp as a mid-level corporate counsel in the late 1980s and was promoted, fitfully but persistently, into the senior executive ring by the late 1990s. He survived four CEO transitions (Norman → Harry → Norman → Normie/board trust → Norman), which is, in itself, diagnostic of unusual political instincts. By the *Goblin Nation* arc, Menken was operating as subject's deputy across the entire Goblin Underground network — a role that required knowing about, and concealing, capital crimes on a daily basis.

**Dynamics.** Subject has used Menken for thirty years as the operational test-case of "sycophancy I despise but require." Menken's fluency in the dialect of executive deference is total; subject reads this fluency as proof of Menken's worthlessness, and uses it. Menken, for his part, has accurately calibrated that the only survival strategy with subject is unconditional, public, repeated demonstration that he is *not* a rival — that he wants the second chair forever, never the first.

**Evolution.** What is striking is that Menken has, against actuarial odds, survived. Most members of subject's inner ring across decades have been killed, imprisoned, or driven to suicide. Menken's longevity is a function of three behaviors: (1) never seeking credit publicly, (2) absorbing blame publicly without complaint, and (3) demonstrating, through small unprompted competences, that his removal would cost the enterprise more than his presence.

**Trust / safety.** Subject "trusts" Menken in the sense that subject knows precisely what Menken will and will not do, and the predictability has held. This is the closest subject comes to trust.

**Failure mode.** Menken will, eventually, make one judgment subject reads as ambition rather than service, and the file will close. The likeliest trigger is a succession scenario in which Menken is briefly the visible face of the company during one of subject's incapacitations; the visibility itself will read as theft.

**Leverage.** For containment: Menken is the single best human asset in subject's environment. He has documentary memory of three decades of crime, has no ideological loyalty to subject, and is plausibly turnable in a witness-protection frame. The window for turning him is during one of subject's incarcerations; the window closes the moment subject is loose.

---

## 7-B.5 — THE THUNDERBOLTS / DARK AVENGERS ROSTER (BULLSEYE, DAKEN, MAC GARGAN, MOONSTONE, ARES, NOH-VARR, THE SENTRY)

**Category.** Constructed "team," chosen-family-by-press-release. Included as a unit because subject's relationship to each member is a variation on a single template: assemble psychopaths I can present as heroes, project my disavowed aggression onto them, and rule from above the wreckage.

**History.** Assembled in the wake of Secret Invasion (2008). Each member was selected for one of three properties: (a) media-trainable resemblance to an existing Avenger (Gargan→Spider-Man, Daken→Wolverine, Moonstone→Ms. Marvel, Bullseye→Hawkeye, Noh-Varr→Captain Marvel); (b) raw destructive utility (Ares, Sentry); or (c) value as a hostage-to-be-managed (the Sentry, whose Void aspect subject calculated he could leverage through Lindy and through pharmacology).

**Dynamics — individual.**

- **Bullseye.** Subject understood Bullseye as a precision instrument with no internal life worth managing. He kept Bullseye on a short chain through small recurring kills — the equivalent of feeding a working dog. Trust: zero, by design. Bullseye knew he was a tool and preferred it.

- **Daken.** Subject recognized in Daken a fellow specimen of paternally-induced damage running an inverted-identification program; the recognition produced a peculiar near-affection, which subject expressed as targeted manipulation. Daken was the only Dark Avenger to whom subject ever spoke in something like a paternal register, and the only one subject was, ultimately, slightly afraid of.

- **Mac Gargan (Venom).** Subject used Gargan as a controlled-symbiote experiment in addition to a Spider-Man surrogate. The contempt was visible to all parties; Gargan accepted it for the costume and the chemical leash.

- **Moonstone (Karla Sofen).** The most dangerous individual on the roster to subject personally, because Sofen is a fellow malignant narcissist with formal clinical training in the manipulation playbook. Their relationship was a continuous low-grade contest of grooming each other; subject won by hierarchy, not by skill. There are reasons to suspect (Ellis run, Bendis run) that subject had a brief sexual involvement with Sofen, which would be in character (sex as power-display, never affect) and which she would have understood identically.

- **Ares.** A pure transactional relationship. Subject paid Ares in war and in his son's tuition. Ares respected subject's willingness to deliver both. There was no warmth and no need for any.

- **Noh-Varr.** Subject misread him entirely, assuming alien naïveté would translate to manageability. Noh-Varr defected the moment he understood the operation. Diagnostically: subject's blindness to ideological motivation in others is a recurring tactical weakness.

- **The Sentry (Robert Reynolds).** The most clinically interesting relationship of the Dark Reign period. Subject identified in Reynolds a psyche even more split than his own, and a power level that, properly handled, was a strategic asset of nuclear scale. Subject pharmacologically and psychologically tended Reynolds — adjusting medications, isolating him from Lindy, feeding his grandiosity, encouraging the Void — with a sustained attentiveness he has shown few other human beings. The motive was instrumental; the *quality of attention* was nonetheless remarkable. Subject understood Reynolds better than Reynolds' wife did, and used the understanding to ruin him.

**Trust / safety.** Calibrated per member, uniformly low, structurally adequate for the operational window (approximately twelve in-universe months).

**Failure mode.** The roster was designed to be disposable, and disposed. The deeper failure was subject's: he confused the manageability of psychopaths with the manageability of public perception, and lost the second.

**Leverage.** For containment: the surviving roster members are durable witnesses against subject and durable competitors for his attention. Any of them returned to his orbit will be both useful intelligence and an accelerant.

---

## 7-B.6 — THE HOOD (PARKER ROBBINS)

**Category.** Subordinate lieutenant during Dark Reign; the closest analogue to a "criminal protégé" subject has accepted.

**History.** Robbins was a small-time criminal elevated by a demonic hood to mid-tier supervillain organizer; subject inherited him as the de facto commissioner of the costumed underworld and kept him there. The relationship was the most overtly *patronage*-shaped relationship of subject's career: subject provided legitimacy and air cover, Robbins provided street-level enforcement and the implicit threat of mobilizing the entire B-list rogues catalogue.

**Dynamics.** Subject treated Robbins with a deliberate, performed respect that was, by Osborn standards, lavish — the equivalent of a senator publicly thanking a county chairman. The performance was intelligible to both men as performance, and functioned. Robbins was never deceived that subject saw him as a peer; Robbins also was never asked to pretend otherwise. Of all subject's Dark Reign relationships, this was the least riddled with idealize-devalue oscillation, because subject never idealized him in the first place.

**Trust / safety.** Stable within transactional terms. Both parties expected betrayal at the appropriate moment and prepared for it.

**Failure mode.** Robbins' demonic patron (Dormammu, later other entities) was a competing principal subject could not control. The relationship's structural failure was therefore exogenous, not interpersonal.

**Leverage.** Robbins remains alive, intermittently powered, and carries detailed knowledge of subject's underworld logistics circa 2009–2010. A turnable asset, but one whose own pathology must be managed in parallel.

---

## 7-B.7 — LILY HOLLISTER ("Menace") and the GABRIEL OSBORN COMPLEX

*Treated structurally under Family in Section 7-A; included here in summary because Hollister was, in her own self-presentation, an "ally" and "partner" before she became the mother of subject's second son.*

The relationship is a compressed Stromm replay with sexual content: idealization (genuine intellectual engagement with Hollister's political ambitions and her own Goblin-Formula derivative), extraction (her body, her father's political machine, a son), devaluation (her supersession by the next operational priority), and disposal (functional abandonment with intermittent control-reassertions). What is notable is the duration: the Hollister "alliance" phase was unusually long for subject (~two years in-universe), suggesting that the prospect of an heir who was *not* Harry — an heir uncontaminated by the Harry-failure narrative — produced a temporary stabilization in subject's affect. The stabilization did not survive Gabriel's birth, at which point the projective complex that has always organized subject's paternity reasserted itself with the new infant in the despised-self slot.

**Leverage.** Hollister, when accessible, is a primary witness, a co-conspirator with her own legal exposure, and a mother whose continued access to Gabriel can be configured as a containment lever. She is not a stable asset on her own terms; she is a usable one in a structured program.

---

## 7-B.8 — THE CABAL (DOOM, NAMOR, EMMA FROST, LOKI, THE HOOD)

**Category.** Peer-tier conspiracy; the only setting in subject's life in which he has, however briefly, occupied a chair at a table of genuine equals.

**Dynamics — composite.** The Cabal is diagnostically illuminating because subject's conduct within it differed sharply from his conduct anywhere else. He did not attempt to dominate Doom; he did not attempt to seduce Frost; he did not attempt to bully Namor. He performed *chairman*, not *predator*. The performance held until it didn't — Loki was manipulating the entire room and subject; Frost and Namor were running an internal counter-op; Doom withdrew the moment subject's HAMMER assets attacked Latveria. The Cabal disintegrated because subject could not sustain the chairman-among-equals posture once stressed, and reverted to dominance behaviors that the other principals would not accept.

**Trust / safety.** None, mutual, understood by all parties as the operating frame.

**Failure mode.** Subject's inability to *not* attempt to become first among ostensible equals. He lost Doom permanently — a strategic blunder of historic scale — by ordering an attack on Latveria as a status display.

**Leverage.** Each of these figures retains a grudge of long-memory caliber. Doom's enmity in particular is a containment asset of the first order and should be tracked.

---

## 7-B.9 — VICTORIA HAND

**Category.** Personally-recruited deputy director, HAMMER; the rarest sub-type in the subject's life — a competent subordinate with whom he had a functional, non-sexual, non-paternal working relationship that he did not sabotage.

**History.** Hand was a mid-level SHIELD bureaucrat subject identified, recruited away, and elevated to deputy director on the basis of pure capability assessment. She was openly skeptical of him, told him so to his face, and was retained precisely because of it. Across the year of HAMMER's existence, Hand was the operational executive who actually ran the agency; subject did the performances, the press, the Cabal, the Dark Avengers, and the visions; Hand kept the lights on.

**Dynamics.** This is the most anomalous file in the entire 7-B section. Subject permitted Hand to disagree with him, to brief him bluntly, to override middle-management decisions without consulting him, and — most strikingly — to leave the building unmonitored. The most parsimonious explanation: subject, in the Iron Patriot period, briefly internalized the executive-reaction-formation identity to the point where he was *playing* a man who would have a Victoria Hand, and the playacting produced a real working partnership inside the performance. It is the closest thing to a non-pathological relationship on his record.

**Evolution.** Hand survived Siege, defected back to the Avengers' side under Captain America, and was eventually killed in an unrelated arc. Subject's reaction to her death is unrecorded, which is itself data.

**Trust / safety.** Functional. Notably, when HAMMER fell, Hand was the one subordinate against whom subject did not retaliate, and whom he did not publicly denounce. This is, for him, the equivalent of a eulogy.

**Failure mode.** None, on the relationship's own terms. It failed because the institution housing it failed.

**Leverage.** The Hand file is the proof-of-concept that subject can, under sufficiently structured institutional incentives and sufficiently calibrated counterpart selection, sustain a functional working relationship with a non-


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

*Section C of the relational map. Family in Part I, professional/operational network in Part II. This section catalogues the antagonists, obsessional objects, and erotic/intimate counterparts — the figures organized around competition, hatred, and (such as it exists in the subject) desire. Note at the outset: for OSBORN these categories bleed into each other. The most intense intimacies of his life are with his enemies; the women he has bedded are largely instruments of rivalry; the rivals function as the only sustained "relationships" in the conventional sense — i.e., people whose existence he tracks, whose absence he registers, whose face he remembers without effort.*

---

## A. THE PRIMARY RIVAL — PETER PARKER / SPIDER-MAN

### History

Initial contact: late adolescence of the rival, *Amazing Spider-Man* #14 (retroactively positioned; the Goblin recruits the Enforcers to bait Spider-Man for filmed combat — note the audience-bid even at first contact). Through the Lee/Ditko/Romita run, escalation across roughly two years of in-universe time culminating in the bridge incident (ASM #121–122), the impalement, the false death, the European exile, the Clone Saga orchestration (1994–96 publication), Revelations, the *Pulse* and *Marvel Knights* run reacquisitions, the *Brand New Day* peripheral involvement, the Dark Reign confrontations, Goblin Nation, the Red Goblin bond, the Kindred entanglement, and the present-day continuing standoff. Total relational duration: longer than either of OSBORN's marriages, longer than his active parenting of Harry, longer than any business partnership, longer than any custodial period in any prison. **It is the longest sustained dyad in subject's life.**

### Dynamics

The relationship is structured as an **inverted family romance**. Subject is approximately the age Peter's father Richard would have been; subject is a captain of industry of the exact type Peter could never become; subject identified Peter under the mask before Peter's wife did. There is a paternal-erotic-annihilatory triple-bind: he wants to be Peter's father, to *replace* Peter's father, to *destroy* what Peter's actual lost fathers (Richard, Ben) gave him, and to be witnessed in the destruction. The Gwen Stacy throw was not an attack on Spider-Man; it was an act performed *for* Spider-Man, addressed to him, requiring his presence. Every subsequent operation against Peter has carried this performative-intimate signature: the kidnapping of Aunt May; the framing of Flash Thompson; the cloning operations; the targeting of MJ; the Red Goblin's serial-attack on every named intimate of Peter Parker in sequence. Subject does not *fight* Peter Parker so much as *court* him through atrocity.

### Evolution

Phase 1 (Ditko era): strategic — Spider-Man is an obstacle to subject's criminal interests. Phase 2 (Romita through Gwen): obsessional — Spider-Man becomes the *meaning* of subject's life as Goblin. Phase 3 (post-122 exile): elaborated and abstracted — subject can engineer Peter's misery from across an ocean, the obsession no longer requiring physical proximity. Phase 4 (post-Revelations): institutional — subject acquires the Bugle, the company, the political position partly to surround Peter with himself. Phase 5 (Dark Reign): inverted — subject occupies Peter's social role (public hero, autograph-signed, photographed) while Peter is fugitive. Phase 6 (Red Goblin/Kindred): regressive-totalizing — direct, simultaneous, undefended attack on every intimate. The evolution is from *predator-and-prey* to *parasite-and-host*: subject increasingly cannot exist without Peter to organize around.

### Trust / Safety

There is, paradoxically, a stable structure of expectation between them. Each knows the other will not, finally, kill him; each knows the other will not, finally, leave him alone. Spider-Man has had OSBORN at point-blank dozens of times and not finished it; OSBORN has had Peter unmasked, drugged, defeated, kneeling, and has reliably escalated to spectacle rather than execution. Safety in the literal sense is zero on both sides. Safety in the relational sense — the certainty of the other's continued, attentive enmity — is total. **Neither has had a more reliable presence in his adult life.**

### Failure Mode

Subject fails in this relationship via the *spectacle-over-victory* compulsion. He has had Peter dead-to-rights at minimum a dozen documented times across the canon. Each time he has chosen to extend, decorate, address, or witness the moment rather than complete it — and each time has lost. The rivalry cannot be won because winning would terminate the only relationship that organizes him.

### Leverage

- *Indifference, performed convincingly.* Peter's persistent capacity to live a loved and ordinary life — to be photographed laughing with his wife, to attend his aunt's birthday — destabilizes subject more than any combat outcome. Any containment strategy that can keep Peter *visibly happy and uninterested* in OSBORN is more damaging to subject than any prison.
- *Anonymity of defeat.* Spider-Man wins that go unreported, that no news camera captures, that no Bugle headline carries — these wound disproportionately.
- *The mutual unmasking.* Subject knowing Peter's name is a one-way intimacy he treasures. Peter publicly knowing and naming OSBORN's *true* organizing wound (the boy in Amberson's house) would be the inverse blow he is least prepared for.

---

## B. THE SECONDARY RIVAL — J. JONAH JAMESON

### History

Acquaintance pre-dates the Goblin formation; subject and Jameson moved in overlapping civic-philanthropic circles in 1960s/70s New York — board dinners, mayoral fundraisers, the kind of room where industrialists and publishers complain about taxes together. Active hostility crystallized when Jameson, post-Revelations, refused to whitewash the Goblin record in his pages — the one editorial line Jameson, for all his Spider-Man derangement, has never crossed. Subject's response was the slow, methodical acquisition of the *Daily Bugle* itself (Stern era, *Pulse* and Bendis follow-through), and the public humiliation of Jameson as publisher in his own building.

### Dynamics

Subject regards Jameson with an interesting and rare emotion: **a contempt mixed with grudging fraternal recognition.** Jameson, like subject, is loud, vain, choleric, obsessed with a single young man in a mask, and unable to let go. The difference, which subject can articulate when sober, is that Jameson is *honest* about his obsession — wears it on his front page — and is, beneath everything, a man with a moral spine. Subject finds the spine particularly insulting because it is housed in a man he otherwise considers his lesser.

### Evolution

Civic-peer (1970s) → editorial nuisance (1980s, post-Revelations) → acquisition target (Stern/Pulse) → owned humiliated subordinate (Bendis) → restored adversary (post-Dark Reign, Jameson having outlived the takeover). Subject has not been able to *destroy* Jameson, partly because Jameson is, in a way subject cannot quite metabolize, indestructible by his methods — you cannot break a man by humiliating him publicly if he humiliates himself daily in 72-point type.

### Trust / Safety

Jameson is the rare antagonist subject does not attempt to physically kill. There is a tacit non-lethal frame, observed by both. Why: killing Jameson would leave subject without the one rival who *understands the Parker fixation from the inside.*

### Failure Mode

Subject consistently underestimates Jameson's capacity to absorb humiliation without changing course. The takeover of the *Bugle* did not break Jameson; it freed him (to found *Front Line*, to enter politics, to continue the Spider-Man crusade through other organs). Subject's leverage model — *take what they love, watch them break* — fails against a man whose self-organization is built around being thwarted.

### Leverage

- *Jameson's wife (Marla, in earlier canon; the second Mrs. Jameson) and son (John Jameson the astronaut).* Subject knows this; has weaponized it tangentially; will again if pressed.
- *Jameson's secret guilt over the original Scorpion creation.* A pressure point subject has filed but not yet fully exploited.

---

## C. THE INSTITUTIONAL RIVAL — ANTHONY E. STARK

### History

Cocktail-circuit acquaintance from the 1980s tech-industry beltway. Subject has *envied* Stark since before there was an Iron Man — envied the inherited fortune (Howard Stark's wealth and approval, the precise twin negatives of Amberson Osborn), envied the press, envied the easy genius. The hostility escalated through the registration era, exploded in *Secret Invasion* when subject pulled the trigger on Veranke and was rewarded with Stark's job, his armor concept, his Tower, his Avengers brand, and (briefly) his global influence. The Iron Patriot armor is the single most diagnostically transparent costume in subject's wardrobe: it is Stark's silhouette painted as Rogers, worn by OSBORN. It says, plainly, *I want to be the man America loves; I will dress as the two men America loves and call it me.*

### Dynamics

This is **envy proper** — Kleinian, corrosive, organized around the perception that Stark possesses goods (fatherly approval, cultural love, effortless brilliance) that subject was unjustly denied. Subject's relationship to Stark is contaminated by this throughout. Even when subject held all the institutional power and Stark was a fugitive with a degraded brain, subject could not stop performing *for* Stark — the Tower occupation, the armor, the public statements were addressed to Stark as much as to the public.

### Evolution

Peer-rival in industry (1980s–2000s) → ideological opposite in Registration → triumphant successor in Dark Reign → defeated and humiliated in Siege → restored as periodic antagonist post-resurrection. The Dark Reign year was, for subject, *the year he was Tony Stark*, and its loss is metabolized as a deeper humiliation than the loss of any of his own roles.

### Trust / Safety

Mutual lethal capacity, mutual non-lethal practice. Stark, characteristically, has tried to *talk* to subject more than once; subject experiences this as condescension and is destabilized by it.

### Failure Mode

Subject is unable to enjoy his Stark-occupations because they remain occupations — he is wearing borrowed clothes and knows it. The envy is never satisfied by acquisition; the acquired object becomes contaminated by having passed through Stark's hands.

### Leverage

- *Stark's sobriety / addiction history.* The one zone where subject has the moral upper hand and uses it relentlessly.
- *Stark's paternal wound (Howard).* Subject has, in private exchanges, probed it. He recognizes the structure because it inverts his own.

---

## D. THE PATRIOTIC RIVAL — STEVEN G. ROGERS

### History

Distal, mostly mediated through the Iron Patriot costume and the Dark Reign appropriation of Avengers symbology. Direct confrontations are fewer than with Stark or Parker, but the *symbolic* relationship is profound: Rogers is the man America loves without irony, the figure subject has spent a career trying to counterfeit.

### Dynamics

Where Stark is envied for the *gifts*, Rogers is envied for the *goodness*. Subject regards Rogers' moral coherence as an unfair advantage — a kind of structural cheating — and has, on several occasions (Siege foremost), attempted to expose Rogers as secretly compromised. Each attempt has failed because Rogers, uniquely among subject's targets, has no concealed shame to surface.

### Trust / Safety

Rogers' restraint toward subject — refusal to kill him in moments where it would have been legally and morally defensible — registers in subject as further humiliation, not mercy. He would prefer Rogers to have killed him at Siege; the alternative is to have been *spared by* Captain America.

### Failure Mode

Cannot be psychologically reached by the attack-the-intimate template because Rogers' intimates (Wilson, Barnes, Romanoff) are themselves combat-capable and Rogers' moral structure does not collapse under personal loss the way subject's would.

### Leverage

- *None reliable.* This is the rare antagonist on whom subject has no working leverage. He compensates with public-relations attacks of decreasing effect.

---

## E. THE MAGICAL/DEMONIC RIVAL — KINDRED (HARRY-IDENTIFIED)

### History

The Kindred entity, in the configuration that emerged through the Spencer run, was constituted from a version of Harry Osborn entangled with Mephistophelean machinery. Subject's relationship to Kindred is therefore the strangest of his life: it is simultaneously a war with his own son, his own sin against his son, and an external supernatural antagonist.

### Dynamics

For perhaps the only time in the record, subject is the *object* of an attack-the-intimate campaign rather than its author. Kindred targeted everyone OSBORN had ever harmed and arranged them for tableau. Subject's response was a confused mix of guilt-affect (genuine, brief, disorientating to him), defensive reformation (the Sin-Eater "purging" arc), and the residual paternal flicker he cannot fully suppress regarding Harry.

### Failure Mode

Subject is structurally unequipped to be a victim. The Kindred arc destabilized him not because of damage inflicted but because it positioned him in the role he had spent his life imposing on others.

### Leverage

- *Subject's residual paternal affect for Harry.* The most reliable single penetration of his defensive structure. Even an enemy wearing Harry's face exploits it.

---

## F. THE OPERATIONAL ENEMIES (compressed)

### Mendel Stromm

The original betrayed mentor — chemistry professor whose research subject stole and whose freedom subject engineered away. Stromm's intermittent returns from the dead and revenge attempts have been, for subject, an embarrassment rather than a threat: Stromm represents the *first* iteration of the predation-on-benefactors pattern, and subject finds the pattern's visible authorship uncomfortable. Leverage on subject: minimal. Subject's leverage on Stromm: total; Stromm has never recovered from the original betrayal and cannot organize sustained opposition.

### Roderick Kingsley (the original Hobgoblin)

A pure rivalry in the *commercial-villain* sense — Kingsley stole subject's identity-of-power (the Goblin formula caches, the equipment) during subject's European exile and built a career on it. Subject regards Kingsley with the contempt one feels for a successful counterfeiter: galling, dismissible, eventually to be liquidated. Kingsley's superior business discipline (he franchises the identity; he protects his real name) is something subject privately recognizes as worth study.

### Doctor Doom

A peer of a different order. Subject regards Doom with wary respect — Doom is, by subject's reckoning, the only other man in his weight class on the dimensions that matter (grandiose-competent, scientifically credible, willing to wear a costume in public). Their Cabal-era collaboration was carefully courteous on both sides because both knew the other was the only person in the room they could not casually destroy. Subject does not provoke Doom; Doom returns the favor. Trust: zero. Stability: high.

### Namor McKenzie

Cabal-era adjacency. Subject regards Namor as a *useful aristocrat* and an inferior strategist. The Emma Frost / Namor defection from the Cabal during Dark Reign was experienced as a personal betrayal subject has not forgotten.

### Loki Laufeyson

The Cabal's wild card. Subject was outplayed by Loki at Siege — manipulated into the Asgard assault that destroyed his career. He recognizes this and carries it. Future contact will be characterized by attempted preemption that Loki will, predictably, anticipate.

### Bullseye / Hawkeye-impersonator (Lester)

A *kept* enemy: a man subject sustained as a weapon during the Dark Avengers period despite knowing Lester was uncontainable. Subject's relationship to Lester is a study in his tolerance for risk when the risk is interesting. He likes Lester in the way one likes a particularly responsive attack dog.

### Daken Akihiro

Another kept piece. Subject identifies in Daken the disavowed-son structure (Wolverine's analog of his own Harry-wound, viewed from the father side) and felt unusual affinity. The affinity was not reciprocated; Daken regarded subject as a useful platform and departed.

### Nick Fury (Sr.)

A standing professional antagonist of the institutional kind. Subject's appropriation of SHIELD into HAMMER was, in part, a personalized attack on Fury — taking his apparatus, demolishing his Helicarriers, exiling his agents. Fury's response (the Secret Warriors program) was the more disciplined campaign, and subject knows it.

### Maria Hill

Subject regards Hill as Fury's executor, with respect for her professionalism and contempt for her loyalty (which he reads as servility). She has filed more accurate operational assessments on him than any other intelligence officer; he has read them.

### Norah Winters / Ben Urich / the *Front Line* press apparatus

Subject's relationship to the investigative press is a study in his impatience with non-physical antagonism. He cannot kill journalists without political cost, cannot bribe the good ones, cannot intimidate Urich (tried), and finds the entire category of opposition tedious. They have done him more sustained damage than most of his costumed enemies.

### Luke Cage and the New Avengers underground

During Dark Reign, the Cage-led Avengers were the persistent insurgency subject could not destroy. He underestimated Cage on class grounds (a recurring tell — subject's class-contempt costs him operationally), and the underestimation is on file.

---

## G. LOVERS AND INTIMATE COUNTERPARTS

A note before the catalogue. Subject's intimate life is, almost without exception, **instrumental.** Sexual and romantic relationships are vectors for acquisition (of property, of leverage over rivals, of heirs) and screens against accusations of unmanliness. Authentic erotic life, to the extent it exists, is sublimated into the Spider-Man rivalry. The women in this section are not, with one exception, persons in subject's interior world; they are roles he has cast.

### Emily Lyman Osborn (deceased; first wife, mother of Harry)

History: courtship during subject's late-twenties consolidation of Oscorp. Emily was, by every surviving account (Harry's reconstructed memories; DeMatteis's "The Child Within"), genuinely loved by subject — or, more precisely, loved as much as subject's structure permits. She was the one figure who saw him without the defensive apparatus engaged. Her death from complications following Harry's birth was, in subject's distorted accounting, an abandonment and a theft: Harry took her, therefore Harry owes her, therefore Harry can never repay. The whole arc of the paternal pathology routes through this displacement.

Trust / safety while living: the one relationship in which subject reliably slept with his back exposed. Failure mode: she died; he did not. Leverage in present day: invocation of Emily is one of the rare names that produces a non-grandiose affect in subject — a brief, dilated pupil, a swallowed breath, a topic change. Operationally significant.

### Lily Hollister ("Menace")

History: Harry's then-girlfriend (*Brand New Day* era, Slott/Gale/McKone). Subject's seduction and impregnation of Lily was a textbook attack-the-intimate maneuver, but with a layered target: it humiliated Harry, established a second son (Gabriel / American Son) as a replacement-extension, and brought a Goblin-enhanced operative into subject's personal control.

Dynamics: Lily was not deceived; she chose subject because subject was, in her assessment, *the actual power*. This mutual instrumentalization is the closest subject has come post-Emily to a partnership based on accurate mutual reading.

Evolution: alliance → operational asset → discarded as Gabriel's existence outlived its utility. Subject does not maintain contact in good standing.

Failure mode: subject cannot sustain partnership with a peer-instrumentalist because he requires the asymmetry of being the one doing the using. Lily's willingness to use him back made her, eventually, intolerable.

Leverage on subject: Gabriel's existence. The "American Son" arc demonstrated that subject regards Gabriel as more disposable than Harry, but disposability is not absence — Gabriel can still be used as a hook.

### Gwen Stacy (alleged; *Sins Past* canon)

Status: contested editorially; treated here as on-file. If the Straczynski-canon account stands, subject's brief affair with Gwen Stacy is the **purest expression** of the attack-the-intimate template applied prospectively: take, from the rival, the woman the rival loves, before the rival can fully have her. The twin children (Sarah and Gabriel Stacy in this continuity) are operational extensions.

Dynamics: predatory in the most clinical sense — an older powerful man identifying a vulnerability window in a young woman connected to his obsession. No reciprocal affect on subject's side beyond conquest.

Leverage: this episode is the single piece of subject's history that, if surfaced widely and credibly, would damage him with constituencies that have tolerated worse — because the optics of the predation are unrecoverable.

### Various transactional liaisons (corporate-era)

Subject has, across the decades, maintained an irregular pattern of short-term liaisons with women associated with rivals (executives' wives at industry functions; once, briefly, a Bugle reporter — pre-acquisition; twice, women in the Oscorp legal department). Pattern is consistent: short duration, no emotional investment, terminated by subject, often weaponized later through hint or document. Operationally these are minor; behaviorally they are confirmatory of the attack-the-intimate signature in low-stakes form.

### The non-relationship with Mary Jane Watson-Parker

Subject has never had a sexual or romantic involvement with MJ and has, by the public record, never seriously attempted one — but the *threat* of such attempt has been a recurrent instrument (the Goblin abductions, the symbiote-era cornerings, the Red Goblin sequence). MJ functions in subject's psychology as **Gwen's surviving avatar** — the woman the rival was permitted to keep — and the inability to take her without prematurely terminating the rivalry is one of the few impulses subject has consistently held in check. The check is strategic, not moral.

Leverage: MJ herself is one of the most acute readers of subject in the canon — she identified the Iron Patriot construct as theatrics with a speed and certainty most analysts did not match. Subject is aware she sees him clearly. He resents it and avoids her gaze when other options exist.

### Aunt May


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: NORMAN VIRGIL OSBORN
## Section VI — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

*An exhaustive longitudinal inventory of subject's operational capability set, sorted by acquisition vector (endogenous → pharmacological → technological → institutional), with mechanism, ceiling, attrition pattern, and — critically — the manner in which each capability is **deformed by character** into a signature. The thesis of this section: subject's powers are individually impressive and collectively redundant, but each one is bent, in use, toward the same psychic end. The capabilities do not determine the man; the man determines the capabilities.*

---

### 1. ENDOGENOUS / PRE-FORMULA SUBSTRATE

#### 1.1 General Intelligence (Premorbid)

Subject's pre-formula cognitive baseline is, on the available record (college performance, Stromm-displacement scheme, founding-era Oscorp portfolio), already markedly superior — conservatively top-percentile general intelligence with particular strength in applied chemistry, mechanical engineering, and adversarial strategic reasoning. The Stromm fraud (academic theft + legal weaponization + corporate capture, executed by a man not yet thirty) is itself a non-trivial operation requiring fluency across three disciplines (organic chemistry, criminal procedure, corporate law) and a long planning horizon. This is the **substrate the formula amplified**; it is not what the formula created.

**Limit at substrate level.** Whatever his pre-formula IQ, subject's reasoning was already bent by character: brilliance in service of acquisition, contempt for collaborative or peer-review modalities, intolerance for any expertise that exceeded his own in a domain he claimed. He could not — cannot — work *with* a true equal; he can only annex, exploit, or destroy them.

#### 1.2 Executive / Industrial Skill

Independent of any superhuman augmentation, subject is a working-class one-percent industrialist: capable of building, running, asset-stripping, hostile-acquiring, and operating at the boardroom-to-Senate interface. He has personally restructured Oscorp through at least four documented near-collapses, weathered SEC and federal scrutiny, performed a friendly takeover of the *Daily Bugle*, and during Dark Reign administered a global paramilitary apparatus (H.A.M.M.E.R.) with multinational footprint, a satellite intelligence service, an Avengers-branded counterforce, and a media operation, simultaneously, for roughly a year — without operational collapse until directly provoked into one. The man can manage organizations.

**Signature distortion.** He cannot delegate without subsequently destroying the delegate. His org charts are functional but high-attrition; the median tenure of a senior Osborn lieutenant before discard, frame, or murder is short by any industry benchmark (Menken, Hollister, Kingsley-adjacent, Bench, Macendale, Lily, the entire Dark Avengers roster). His executive talent is real; his executive **stability** is character-limited.

#### 1.3 Combat Substrate (Pre-Formula)

Minimal. The pre-explosion Norman is not documented as a trained fighter. All combat capability is downstream of the formula and of post-formula self-training (see §3).

---

### 2. THE GOBLIN FORMULA — PHARMACOLOGICAL AUGMENTATION

The single most consequential variable in the file. Aerosolized exposure to a modified Stromm Serum #4 during laboratory detonation; subject has continued, with full knowledge, to self-administer refined and reformulated versions across decades. Effects are best parsed into **physical**, **cognitive**, and **psychiatric** axes.

#### 2.1 Physical Augmentation

- **Strength.** Lift/press capability in the upper "enhanced human" tier, reliably documented at approximately the **9–10 ton** band when fully dosed and rested. He has traded blows with Spider-Man, the Thing (briefly), Luke Cage, and the post-resurrection Captain America at this tier. He is *not* in the Hulk/Thor/Sentry weight class and knows it — his combat doctrine accounts for this asymmetry (see §6).
- **Speed and reflexes.** Sub-Spider-Man but markedly superhuman; sufficient to parry Spider-sense-mediated reactions intermittently. His reflex envelope is the floor that makes glider-piloting at speed survivable.
- **Durability.** Substantially enhanced; he has absorbed point-blank explosions, glider impalement through the thorax, building collapses, and unaugmented small-arms fire without lasting injury. **Hard ceiling:** he is not invulnerable — bladed weapons, sufficiently large kinetic events, and other enhanced-class combatants can wound and have wounded him. His durability is **functional**, not impervious.
- **Healing.** Accelerated — order-of-magnitude faster than baseline. The glider through the chest (ASM #122) is the canonical demonstration: a wound that would kill any unenhanced man closed sufficiently for ambulatory escape and clandestine transport. Healing is the capability that **enabled the Clone Saga**: without it, there is no resurrection arc, no offstage decade, no return.
- **Decelerated senescence.** Subject has presented as a vigorous late-middle-aged man across more than half a century of publication time. Endocrine clock is dramatically suppressed.
- **Stamina.** Functionally tireless across a normal combat envelope; sleep requirement reduced, fatigue threshold elevated.

#### 2.2 Cognitive Augmentation

- **General intelligence elevated.** Post-formula, subject operates at genius-tier across multiple hard sciences. His personal research output spans applied genetics (Goblin Formula variants, the Gathering of Five-era work, the Sin-Eater serum, contributions to the cloning program), advanced robotics (the glider platform across generations, the Goblin drones, the pumpkin-bomb chemistry), neurochemistry (memory manipulation of Peter Parker, mind-control variants used at Oscorp), and weapons miniaturization.
- **Planning horizon extended.** Pre-formula schemes were measurable in months; post-formula operations extend to **years** (the Clone Saga is the seven-plus-year benchmark; Dark Reign is a multi-year arc from American election to Asgard).
- **Working memory and parallel-track cognition.** During Dark Reign he simultaneously managed Doom, Namor, Emma Frost, Loki, the Hood, an Avengers team of unstable psychopaths, a federal agency, and a public-relations persona, without observable executive overload until terminal narcissistic injury.

#### 2.3 Psychiatric Cost — The Inseparable Side Effect

The formula does not have a pharmacological "clean" mode. Every documented dose produces, in proportion: paranoid amplification, grandiosity amplification, sadistic affect, and the loosening of inhibitions that permits the Goblin presentation. He has known this since at least the second decade of the record and has chosen the trade every time. **The formula is not a power he possesses; it is a power he is married to.**

**Hard limits of the pharmacological tier:**
- Forced abstinence (Raft confinement, Sin-Eater purge) produces somatic withdrawal *and* identity collapse. He is dependent.
- Synergistic exposures are catastrophic: the Carnage symbiote bond (Red Goblin) produced a presentation closer to spree-killer than executive, with markedly degraded planning and elevated raw output — a poor trade he nonetheless accepted because it offered a clean shot at every Parker intimate simultaneously.
- Dose-response is non-linear at the upper end. He has overdosed, with transient psychotic dilation, on at least two documented occasions.

---

### 3. ACQUIRED COMBAT SKILL

A frequently underestimated capability layer. Subject is **not** a born fighter; he is a chemist and an industrialist who, after acquiring the substrate, deliberately trained himself into a competent enhanced-tier combatant. The training is self-directed, idiosyncratic, and biased toward the airborne-glider style — but it is real.

- **Striking.** Adequate, brawler-grade, with the formula doing most of the work. He does not have the technical striking of a trained martial artist; he hits hard because he is strong.
- **Bladed weapons.** Notable proficiency with short-blade weapons concealed in the glider's hard points and in the costume gauntlets — see §4.
- **Aerial combat doctrine.** Here he is genuinely innovative. The glider is not a transport platform; it is a combat platform, and subject has developed a doctrine of three-dimensional engagement (strafing, dive-attack, drop-and-bomb, hostage-extraction-from-altitude) that very few opponents in his weight class are equipped to counter. Spider-Man, who is constitutionally an *anchored* combatant (needs surfaces to web from), has spent fifty years adapting to this asymmetry and still struggles in open-sky engagements.
- **Demolitions and incendiaries.** Self-taught to expert level via the chemistry substrate.

**Growth curve.** Combat competence rises steeply through the first decade of activity, plateaus in the middle period, and during Dark Reign visibly *erodes* — he had not been doing his own fighting for some time, and the Iron Patriot phase reveals a man who has outsourced kinetic work to subordinates and atrophied accordingly. Post-Siege he re-acquires baseline through reluctant necessity.

---

### 4. TECHNOLOGY — THE GOBLIN ARSENAL

A continuously iterated, personally engineered weapons portfolio. The notable point: subject **designs, builds, maintains, and upgrades the kit himself**. He does not subcontract; he does not trust. The Goblin gear is one of the few domains where his pathological refusal to delegate produces actual operational advantage — a consistent, single-author weapon system with no leaks and no third-party knowledge.

#### 4.1 The Glider

Successive generations: bat-wing rigid platform → goblin-head VTOL → modular drone-capable hardpoint platform (Dark Reign and after). Capabilities across the line include sustained flight in the 90 mph baseline / dive-burst higher, hover, gyrostabilized one-foot riding posture, weapons hardpoints fore and aft, and — in later iterations — autonomous return-to-pilot homing. The glider is also a **weapon of impalement**, used as such repeatedly (ASM #122 in both directions; later against Flash Thompson; against multiple Spider-allies).

#### 4.2 Pumpkin Bombs

Signature throwable. Standard yield is grenade-class concussive; variants include incendiary, ghost-image / hallucinogen ("Goblin gas"), EMP, smoke, and the so-called *razor bats* (homing bladed projectiles thrown in volleys from the same belt). Chemistry is proprietary and has resisted reverse-engineering by SHIELD and Stark labs across decades.

#### 4.3 Goblin Gas

Multiple formulations. The most diagnostically significant is the **memory-modification aerosol** used on Peter Parker in *Revenge of the Green Goblin* — a chemical instrument of psychological torture, not battlefield use. The fact that this exists in the arsenal at all is itself a piece of the personality file: he engineered a weapon specifically for the project of *making the rival doubt his own mind*. Other formulations produce hallucinogenic terror, paralytic incapacitation, and laughter (a particularly cruel item used episodically).

#### 4.4 Gauntlet Weapons

Finger-tip electrostatic discharge ("Goblin sparks") at sub-lethal-to-lethal range; concealed retractable blades; bola launchers in some iterations.

#### 4.5 Iron Patriot Armor (Dark Reign era)

A Stark-tier exoskeleton, modified by subject from captured Iron Man chassis and re-skinned in red-white-blue Captain America livery. Capabilities approach the contemporary Iron Man baseline: flight, repulsor and unibeam output, life support, computer suite, sensor array. Subject's engineering competence to maintain and operate this suit at the level demonstrated is non-trivial; the suit is also, of course, the perfect **symptom-object** — a literal fusion of his envy of Stark with his envy of Rogers, worn as a uniform (see §7).

#### 4.6 Goblin Cyborgs / Goblin Nation / Drone Armies

In the later period he scales: cybernetic Goblin underlings, a foot-army of Goblin-themed enhanced personnel ("Goblin Nation"), and remote-piloted drone swarms. His comfort with mass production indicates the underlying competence; his choice to brand them all as Goblins indicates the underlying narcissism.

---

### 5. INSTITUTIONAL POWERS

Capabilities that are not him but are *exercised through him*, and which at peak rivaled or exceeded his personal combat tier in real-world consequence.

- **Oscorp Industries.** A multinational chemical/biotech/defense conglomerate. R&D pipeline includes the dominant Goblin Formula variants, applied genetics, miniaturized weapons systems, urban surveillance contracts, and segments of the New York municipal infrastructure.
- **The *Daily Bugle* (Stern/Slott eras).** Acquired in part as instrument for ruining Jameson, in part as megaphone — a private narrative engine.
- **H.A.M.M.E.R. (Dark Reign).** Successor agency to SHIELD, federally chartered, globally deployed, with intelligence, paramilitary, and superhuman-asset arms. At peak roughly equivalent to Stark/Fury-era SHIELD in capability, though substantially shorter-lived and more brittle organizationally.
- **The Dark Avengers / Thunderbolts.** A directly controlled black-ops superhuman team — the operational expression of his ability to recruit, channel, and (briefly) command other severely disordered enhanced individuals via flattery, leverage, and shared contempt.
- **Political access.** Across decades, sustained influence at federal and (during Dark Reign) executive level. Subject is one of relatively few Marvel antagonists who has held *legitimate* power, and the file should note this is itself a capability — he can pass.

**Signature limit at institutional tier.** Every Osborn institutional capability has collapsed at roughly the same point on the same curve: peak capability ≈ 12–18 months, terminal failure at the next narcissistic injury, because he cannot subordinate the personal psychodrama to the institutional life. H.A.M.M.E.R. died at Asgard because *he* needed to be at Asgard.

---

### 6. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS — HOW HE ACTUALLY USES WHAT HE HAS

The capabilities above are the inventory. The following are the **patterns of use** repeated across the record, in which the man becomes legible through the weapon.

#### 6.1 Attack-the-Intimate as Doctrine

Given an enhanced-strength body, a flying weapons platform, the world's deadliest grenades, and a chemistry lab, the most rational use against Spider-Man would be: ambush, overwhelming force, immediate kill. He has had this option dozens of times. He has, with rare exceptions, declined it. The doctrinal preference is *kidnap the loved one, transport to a symbolic location (a bridge, a clock tower, a hospital), force the rival to arrive in distress, then perform the destruction in his presence.* This is not tactically optimal; it is **the only thing the capability is for**. The arsenal exists to enable spectacle against an audience of one.

#### 6.2 The Reveal

A second consistent application: **make sure the rival knows it is you**. The Goblin mask comes off in private at the moment of revelation. He cannot enjoy a victory the loser does not understand. This is why he was the first villain to identify Peter Parker — not as intelligence triumph but as *intimacy demand*.

#### 6.3 The Long Operation

He scales his planning horizon directly to the importance of the target. Random opponent: minutes. Business rival: weeks. Spider-Man: years, decades, generations. The Clone Saga is the purest expression: technical capability (cloning, memory manipulation, identity engineering, distributed cell management) exhaustively deployed in service of a single project — *make Peter Parker doubt that he is Peter Parker*. There is no economic motive. There is only the project.

#### 6.4 The Persona Switch as Tactical Asset

Subject uses the Norman/Goblin distinction operationally. The Norman presentation deflects legal, social, and superhuman attention; the Goblin presentation discharges aggression and terrifies witnesses. He moves between them in deliberate cadence: Norman to the boardroom, Goblin to the rooftop, Norman to the courtroom, Goblin to the holding cell when the cameras are off. Counter-intelligence note: any containment regime that does not anticipate the switch will be defeated by it.

#### 6.5 Resource Conversion

He routinely converts each capability tier into the next: chemistry → formula → strength → industrial leverage → political access → institutional power → media narrative → political access (reinforced loop). The loop is self-sustaining as long as he can prevent any single tier from being externally audited. When auditing breaks the loop (Skrull invasion creates the opening for the H.A.M.M.E.R. directorate; Siege closes it), the entire stack unwinds at once.

---

### 7. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

Every signature in the kit is a tell. The dossier closes this section by reading the capability set as **diagnostic artifact**.

- **The Goblin aesthetic itself.** A grown industrialist's chosen self-image is a *cackling green imp*: the grotesque, the demonic, the unmistakably *child-frightening*. He has dressed himself, deliberately, as the thing a small boy would fear in a dark room — and then taken that costume into the night to inflict on others the fear he was once made to feel. The costume is a confession.
- **The laugh.** A capability in its own right, weaponized for terror, and at the same time the involuntary discharge phenomenon of a man whose affect regulation fails under arousal. He cannot *not* laugh in those moments. The Goblin's terrifying signature is also the man's incontinent symptom.
- **The glider.** Of all the platforms an enhanced industrialist could choose, he selected one that **puts him above** every opponent, every crowd, every city. The aerial preference is a literalized superiority claim. Notably, when grounded he is materially less effective; when elevated he is more so. The psychology and the kinematics agree.
- **The pumpkin bomb.** A *toy*. A children's holiday object refashioned to maim. The man cannot weaponize without theatrical decoration; pure utility offends him. Every armament in his kit has a face.
- **The Iron Patriot armor.** The single most over-determined object in the file. He took Tony Stark's suit (envy of the man who has what he wants), painted it as Captain America (envy of the man who is loved as he is not), and called himself a Patriot (reaction formation against the awareness that he is the country's enemy). It is not a weapon; it is a *résumé*, worn.
- **The memory-modification gas.** He built a chemical to make Peter Parker doubt his own reality. There is no battlefield application. The weapon exists because the project exists. The arsenal documents the obsession.
- **The serum dependence.** He could, at any point in the last forty years, have ceased self-administering the substance that makes him psychotic. He has not. The dependence is not pharmacological alone; the formula is the **chemical signature of refusal to be unaugmented**, i.e., of refusal to be the small boy. The substance is, in his internal economy, the chemistry of *not being Amberson's son*. Of all his powers, this is the one he will surrender last, because surrendering it is surrendering the entire compensatory architecture.

---

### 8. CONTAINMENT-RELEVANT CAPABILITY LIMITS (Summary)

For the operational reader, the consolidated ceiling map:

1. **Combat tier.** Enhanced-human / low-superhuman. Loses to true heavy-hitters (Thor, Hulk, Sentry, peak Stark) in straight engagements; can defeat Spider-Man-class opponents through doctrine and asymmetry but not reliably through force.
2. **Cognitive tier.** Genius-grade, but **brittle** in the Parker-adjacent domain. Reasoning collapses to fixed scripts when the obsessional object is in play.
3. **Institutional tier.** Capable of building agency-scale power; *incapable* of sustaining it past the next narcissistic injury. Operating half-life on any institution he runs solo: roughly 12–18 months.
4. **Pharmacological tier.** Augmentation is real and persistent, but dependence is total; forced sobriety is a viable but high-risk lever and produces extreme behavioral instability before stabilization.
5. **Technological tier.** Self-engineered arsenal of high quality and excellent operational security (single author, no leaks). Replacement-rate after seizure is high; he rebuilds quickly.
6. **Psychological tier.** Witness-dependent. Deny him spectacle and the entire stack degrades.

The capability inventory is formidable. The capability **usage** is the seam. He will always, eventually, choose the personally satisfying application over the operationally optimal one — because the operationally optimal one would not, in the end, make Amberson Osborn's son feel any larger.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — OSBORN, NORMAN V.

*File section 6 of 11. Cross-reference: §1 (History), §3 (Psychological), §5 (Personality). All operational inferences derive from documented behavior across the canonical record; where pattern-extrapolation is used it is marked.*

---

## 6.1 DECISION ARCHITECTURE

Subject does not make decisions the way most executives or most operators make decisions. The conventional model — gather inputs, weigh options, select — is observable only in the surface layer of his behavior, the layer he shows to boards, juries, and adversaries trying to read him. Underneath, decision-making in Osborn is organized along three simultaneous axes that almost never appear separately on-panel:

**Axis A — The Instrumental Stack.** A genuinely high-functioning strategic-planning capacity, comparable to top-decile corporate raiders or intelligence chiefs. Multi-year horizons (the Clone Saga as offstage architecture, the positioning that led to the Iron Patriot appointment, the Goblin Nation seedings). Subject runs decision trees with explicit branch-pruning, contingency-stacking, and burn-down fallbacks. The Stromm acquisition (chemistry → embezzlement frame → corporate seizure) at age 20-something is the prototype: three sequenced moves, each enabling the next, with the optics of legitimacy preserved at every step.

**Axis B — The Narcissistic Audit.** Every decision is silently scored against the question *does this make me larger or smaller in the eyes of the people whose witness I require?* This is not vanity in the trivial sense; it is the operating system. Strategically sound moves that would diminish his visible stature are routinely rejected. Strategically catastrophic moves that promise a symbolic enlargement are routinely taken (throwing Gwen Stacy from the bridge had no tactical payoff and high tactical cost; it was Axis-B-pure). The Iron Patriot armor itself is an Axis-B artifact: a less-functional aesthetic-political composite chosen over the strictly superior Goblin glider/suit because the audience required it.

**Axis C — The Parker Subroutine.** A dedicated, walled, partially autonomous decision engine that fires whenever Peter Parker (or any proxy thereof) enters the operational frame. It overrides both A and B. When the Parker subroutine is hot, Osborn will sacrifice empires for symbolic blows. Anyone running him as an asset or attempting to contain him must model this as a separate decision-maker sharing his body.

**Output behavior of the stack.** In any given operation, A drafts the plan, B edits it for stature, C breaks it under stress. The signature is plans that are 80% rigorous and 20% theatrical, with the theatrical 20% concentrated at the moments of greatest exposure — the moments he treats as performance. Containment forecasters should expect a beautifully engineered operation to collapse at the climax into a glider-cackle moment whose only function is to be seen.

---

## 6.2 PLANNING METHOD AND TIME HORIZON

Subject plans across four characteristic horizons:

- **Strategic (multi-year).** Always at least one such operation running offstage. Documented examples: the post-#122 Europe years building the Clone Saga; the post-Skrull-shot consolidation of HAMMER; the slow-seeded Goblin Nation cells; the maneuvering toward each prison escape. He treats these as portfolios, not single threads — multiple long campaigns running concurrently, each redundant against the others.
- **Operational (weeks to months).** Specific campaigns: a Bugle acquisition arc, a board-replacement, the cultivation of a Hollister, the grooming of a Menken-type apparatchik. Run with formal milestone discipline. He uses calendars, timelines, dossiers — *literal* dossiers; he is a paper-and-screen man, file-keeper.
- **Tactical (days).** Specific assaults, kidnappings, framings. These are usually pre-staged so that the trigger is small and the response large.
- **Reactive (minutes).** Combat tempo. Here the Goblin substrate takes over — improvisation, theatricality, exploitation of terrain, hostage logic.

**Pre-mortems.** Subject is observed, especially in the Stern/DeMatteis and Bendis runs, to rehearse failure conditions explicitly. He pre-stages alibis, body doubles, decoy corpses (he is the only Marvel villain to have effectively faked his own death for two decades of publication), pre-recorded statements, and "discovered" documents that re-frame his actions after the fact. Pre-mortem discipline is a tell of the controlled-CEO mode; its absence is a tell that he has slipped into the Goblin mode.

**Use of redundancy.** Every important capability is held in at least two channels. Funding through licit and illicit conduits both. Glider hardware in multiple safe-houses. Formula stocks split between Oscorp facilities, off-books labs, and personally hidden caches. Information networks split between Oscorp Corporate Intelligence, paid informants in the press (Bugle-era), and his own surveillance product. He learned redundancy from the loss of the original Oscorp facility and has never been observed running single-thread again.

---

## 6.3 TRADECRAFT — INTELLIGENCE AND SURVEILLANCE

Osborn is, in operational-tradecraft terms, an exceptionally capable amateur with billionaire-grade resources who has accreted intelligence-professional habits across decades of contact with SHIELD, HYDRA, the CIA, and during the HAMMER period, the full inheritance of SHIELD's apparatus.

**Collection.** Multi-source by preference. He runs HUMINT (paid informants in newsrooms, in the NYPD, in rival corporations, in Avengers-adjacent staff during HAMMER); SIGINT (Oscorp-developed intercept hardware; during HAMMER, inherited SHIELD product); OSINT (newspaper ownership turns this from collection into manufacture); and what is best called *intimate* intelligence — surveillance of the home, the bedroom, the school of a target's child. The latter is his signature. He does not surveil Peter Parker the operator; he surveils Aunt May's kitchen, MJ's auditions, the baby's room.

**Analysis.** Personally done. He does not delegate analytical judgment on the targets he cares about. This is both a strength (no analyst-bias filter, direct contact with raw product) and a weakness (his Parker-Subroutine corrupts every dataset that touches the fixation).

**Tradecraft hygiene — strong:** compartmentation across his own organizations (Oscorp officers did not know about Goblin operations; HAMMER agents did not know about parallel personal ops); use of cut-outs (Roderick Kingsley, the Menken-types, the Hollister grooming); careful legend-construction for false flags; effective use of body doubles and faked deaths.

**Tradecraft hygiene — weak:** he cannot resist signing his work. The pumpkin bomb, the glider silhouette, the laugh, the specific orange-and-purple chromatic — these are signature tells he will not suppress even when operational logic demands it. During Dark Reign he managed several months of suppressed signature; the suppression itself is what made it remarkable.

---

## 6.4 OPERATIONAL METHODS — REPERTOIRE

Across the record, Osborn's operational repertoire clusters into approximately twelve recurring methods, executed with variations:

1. **The benefactor predation.** Identify a person to whom subject owes a debt of access, knowledge, or capital; extract the asset; destroy the person's standing so the extraction is unrecoverable. *Cases: Stromm; Kingsley as cut-out; Stark's job; Harry's inheritance reversals; the use and abandonment of Menken.*
2. **The intimate strike.** Attack a rival not at the rival but at what the rival loves. *Cases: Gwen; Aunt May; MJ; Flash Thompson as second Goblin frame; baby May Parker; Norah Winters; the entirety of Red Goblin.*
3. **The legitimacy capture.** Acquire a media or governmental platform and use it to invert the subject's public narrative. *Cases: Bugle acquisition; HAMMER directorship; the Iron Patriot persona.*
4. **The proxy/franchise.** License the Goblin identity, the formula, or related capabilities to disposable agents who absorb risk and confuse attribution. *Cases: Bart Hamilton; the Hobgoblin program via Kingsley; the Gobby-Knights and Goblin Nation foot-soldiery; the Dark Avengers as projection-as-policy.*
5. **The grooming-and-promotion.** Cultivate an unstable, vulnerable, or ambitious lieutenant; convince them they are loved or chosen; deploy them; abandon them. *Cases: Lily Hollister; the Hollister pregnancy; multiple Bugle staff; Victoria Hand at the meta-level (she was not fooled but was used).*
6. **The faked death.** Used at least twice for major operational gain; standing in his contingency stack at all times.
7. **The frame.** Construction of evidence-trails implicating others in his crimes. *Cases: Stromm; Flash Thompson; Spider-Man during Dark Reign; assorted Bugle staff.*
8. **The long humiliation.** Multi-year sustained campaign to degrade a rival's sense of reality rather than defeat the rival directly. *Cases: Clone Saga; Kindred-adjacent manipulations; Goblin Nation's targeting of the Otto-Spider-Man.*
9. **The hostage-spectacle.** Combat staged as theatre, with a non-combatant as the lever and the public as the audience. *Cases: Gwen on the bridge; the warehouse hostage scenes recurrent across the Romita-Stern-DeMatteis runs; the Siege climaxes.*
10. **The chemical/biological intervention.** Direct use of his core competency. *Cases: the formula itself in its many iterations; weaponized variants given to Harry, to Hollister, to others; symbiote-vectored attack in Red Goblin.*
11. **The institutional infiltration.** Place his people inside opposing institutions before opposition begins. *Cases: HAMMER cells embedded across federal agencies that outlasted his directorship; Oscorp moles in SHIELD across decades.*
12. **The self-resurrection narrative.** When defeated, return not as a fugitive but as a *reformed* figure, often with documentation, witnesses, and legal counsel pre-arranged. *Cases: post-#122 European return; post-Siege rehabilitation maneuvers; post-Red-Goblin "purified" Osborn in the Spencer run.*

These twelve are the alphabet. The operations are sentences built from them.

---

## 6.5 COMBAT TRADECRAFT

In the field as the Goblin, Osborn's combat doctrine is distinct from his strategic doctrine and must be read as a separate skill set.

**Mobility.** The glider is doctrine, not vehicle. He fights vertical: takes altitude, forces the rival to engage upward into his arsenal, drops at advantageous angles. He treats rooftops, bridges, towers, and atria as preferred terrain and is observably uncomfortable in tight horizontal spaces (subway interiors, basements, sewer engagements — see early Romita work).

**Arsenal.** Layered: incendiary pumpkins; razor-bats; a finger-blaster electrical discharge (gauntlet-mounted); smoke and gas grenades, several with custom psychoactive payloads; the glider's own blades. He almost always carries at least one non-lethal capture round, because the operational goal is rarely simple kill — it is acquisition, terror, or display.

**Engagement preference.** Ambush over duel. He does not seek symmetric combat. He prefers to strike a tired, distracted, or grieving rival, and to begin with a hostage on the table. Direct duels happen only when forced or when the narcissistic audit demands them.

**Disengagement.** He breaks contact early and often. Across the canon he has fled more fights than he has won outright; the fleeing is operationally correct (preserves the asset that is himself) and he does not feel humiliation about it in the moment — humiliation arrives later, in private, and metabolizes into the next operation.

**Lethality discipline.** Asymmetric. With non-rival targets he is casually lethal and indifferent. With the rival himself he is *deliberately* non-lethal across most of the record; killing Peter Parker would terminate the relationship that organizes his life. He will harm any number of others around the rival to preserve this distinction.

---

## 6.6 RESOURCES AND FINANCES

**Licit base — Oscorp Industries.** Diversified industrial conglomerate, originally chemistry-anchored, expanded across defense contracting, robotics, biotech, pharmaceuticals, aerospace, and during the HAMMER period, security services. Public-market exposure varies by era; subject prefers concentrated personal control via trust structures and at least one offshore holding layer. He has been ousted from the company more than once and has recovered control more than once, which establishes that the Oscorp asset is not strictly necessary to him — it is preferred, not load-bearing.

**Illicit base.** Decades of involvement in the New York organized criminal economy, beginning in the Lee/Romita era as a costumed organizer of existing crews and persisting as a quiet equity position in trafficking, weapons, and protection. Income is moved through Oscorp vendor relationships, art and real-estate transactions, and at the Bugle-era peak, advertising and media flows. He has had at least one tame law firm and at least one tame bank in every era.

**Governmental capture.** During Dark Reign, the entire federal national-security budget passed within reach. He skimmed not money — money he had — but *capability*: personnel, technology, classified files, surveillance access. The most operationally significant residue of the HAMMER period is not financial but informational; he walked out of Avengers Tower with the contents of his head, which included identifying information on most of the superhuman community.

**Personal financial habits.** Frugal in the petty register, lavish in the symbolic register. He does not waste money on hedonics — he does not gamble, does not maintain a yacht-and-actresses lifestyle, does not collect for collection's sake. He spends on: the residence (signal of stature), the laboratory (signal of capability), tailored suits (signal of self-discipline), and the symbolic acquisitions that humiliate rivals (the Bugle to humiliate Jameson, the armor to humiliate Stark, the Tower to occupy what was Captain America's). His expenditure pattern is an X-ray of his pathology.

**Cash discipline.** Maintains pre-positioned cash, identity documents, and weapon caches across at least the Eastern Seaboard, and inferentially in Europe (the post-#122 years) and in select Latin American jurisdictions. Pattern-extrapolation: he has never been observed stranded without resources, which means the caches exist and are kept current.

---

## 6.7 INFRASTRUCTURE

**Primary facilities.**
- The Oscorp tower and its R&D campuses (the public face).
- A rotating set of off-books laboratories in the New York metro and at least one in upstate New York, used for formula synthesis and Goblin-equipment manufacture. Locations change every few years; the pattern is that they are leased through shell entities and abandoned at the first sign of compromise.
- Multiple Goblin lairs, hidden in warehouses, sub-basements, and (canonically) in the disused tunnels and subterranean infrastructure of New York. Each is keyed to a particular operational era. He does not return to a burned lair.
- Residential properties — at least one townhouse-style primary residence and several safe-houses, including (varying by era) Long Island and Westchester properties.

**Vehicles.** Glider primary; conventional sedan (chauffeured) for the public role; access to corporate aircraft; during HAMMER, the full SHIELD/HAMMER air fleet. He is competent to pilot the glider obviously and inferentially competent with conventional aircraft.

**Communications.** Compartmentalized. The public Norman runs a normal executive comm profile (assistants, scheduled calls, written correspondence). The Goblin operates from burner-equivalents and from custom Oscorp-built encrypted channels. During HAMMER he had clean access to federal cryptographic resources and inferentially retained custom keys post-removal.

**Personnel infrastructure.** A consistent stratum of fixers, lawyers, PR operatives, and corporate-intelligence officers. Names rotate; the function is stable.
